The Linguistic-Legal Nexus: Why 'Hamidan' as a Hal Clause
Explaining the author's choice of 'حامدا' as a hal clause in the opening

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi usul author used the hal construction 'hamidan' rather than a separate sentence, and identify the hadith-based rationale for equating tasmiyah and tahmid as conditions for beginning an action.

Core Idea
The hal clause 'hamidan' equates tasmiyah and tahmid as simultaneous conditions for beginning.

This lesson examines a subtle but significant choice in the opening of a Hanafi fiqh text. The author could have written a separate sentence praising Allah, but instead used the circumstantial clause 'hamidan'. The commentator's explanation reveals that this is no mere stylistic preference; it reflects a deliberate effort to align the text's linguistic form with a legal principle derived from a hadith: that every important action should begin with both tasmiyah and tahmid. By using the hal, both become simultaneous conditions governing the beginning, emphasizing their equal necessity. This analysis demonstrates how Hanafi usul scholars read legal intent into grammatical structures.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grammatical construction
Recognize that 'hamidan' is a hal clause, a circumstantial accusative describing the state of the subject while performing the action. The alternative would be a separate sentence like 'I praise Allah' (ahmadullah).
2
Understand the author's purpose: taswiyah
The commentator states the author aimed for taswiyah (equalization) between tasmiyah and tahmid. Both should be conditions for the beginning, not one subordinated to the other.
Taswiyah is achieved by making both elements hal clauses attached to the same hidden pronoun.
3
Connect to the hadith evidence
The author's motivation is grounded in a hadith that encourages both tasmiyah and tahmid at the start of actions. The hal construction makes both conditions simultaneous and equally necessary.
The hadith is cited as evidence for the legal requirement of both at the beginning.
4
Draw the legal implication
By using the hal, the author linguistically mirrors the legal principle: the beginning of any significant act should be conditioned by both praising Allah and invoking His name. Without these, the beginning is not considered valid.
This shows how linguistic form can reinforce legal norms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بِسمِ اللهِ الرَّحْمَنِ الرَّحِيمِ
حامد الله تعالى اولا وثانيا ولسان الثناء اليه ثانياه وعلى افضل رسله محمد واله مصليات وفي حلبة الصلوات مجليا ومصلياه حال من المستکن الخ یعنی لفظ حامدا ترکیبی لحاظ سے حال ہے اس ضمیر سے جو باشم کے متعلق یعنی ابتدئی میں مستکن اور ستر ہے اسی ابتدی الکتاب حامدا - ابتدی کا مفعول ذکر کر کے اشارہ کیا کہ حقیقت بہ اللہ کی با ظرف لغو صله ابتدی ہو کر واقع موقع المفعول به نہیں دور نہ تو معنی یہ ہوگا کہ شروع کرتا ہوں تعمیر کو کتاب کی ابتدار تو بالتسمیہ نہ ہوئی حالانکہ مقصود ثانی ہے ۔ بلکہ در حقیقت بار کا متعلق متبرکا ہے جس کے اندر لفظ ابتدی حامل ہے ۔ معنی یہ ہوگا کہ مستر کا بالله ابتدئ الكتاب - اسی طرح حامدا حال ہوگا است رتی کی ضمیر ستان سے اور یہ دونوں حال ابتدئی کی قیدیں ہونگی حامرا معنی ہوگا کہ اسم اللہ کیساتھ تبرک اور اللہ کے لئے حمد کرنے کی حالت میں ابتدائے کتاب کر رہا اشر طريقة الحال - یعنی اس مقام افتتاح اور ابتداء میں طریق متعارف جملہ ہمیر ہوں۔ احمد احمد اللہ یا جلہ فعلیہ احمد اللہ بولنے کا تھا تو اس کو ترک کر کے طریق حال و اختیار کیا اس کی وجہ ہے کہ تشویہ بين الحمد ابو تا که حمد و تسمیہ کے درمیان تسویہ دوبرابری رہے اور رعایتہ تناسب بھی برقرار رہے تویہ سے مراد تو یہ فی امید یہ ہے یعنی حمد اور تسمیہ یہ دونوں ابتداء کی قید ہو جائیں اور وہ ان دونوں سے مقید ہو جائے اور رعایہ تناسب سے مراد یہ ہے دنوں قیدیں ایک ہی جنس سے ہو جائیں یعنی جیسے بالشم مستر کا کے ساتھ متعلق ہو کر حال ہے اسی طرح تحمید بھی حامد کی صورت میں حال آجائے تو اس وقت ابتدار مقید بقید میں ہو جائے گا تو مقصود یہ ہوگا کہ ابتداء کے لئے یہ دونوں قیدیں ضروری ہیں ان کے بدون ابتدار معتبر یہ مستر نہیں ہے ۔ فقد روى في الحديث الذيہ تسمیہ اور تحمید میں مساوات کرنے کی مجھ یش کر رہا ہے مقصد یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں چونکہ تسمیہ اور تحمید دونوں کو ابت رائے فعل میں ضروری قرار دیا گیا ہے اس لئے اس تویہ نے القیدیہ کو اختیار کیا اور ان دونوں کو بصورت حال ابتداء کی قید بنا دیا ۔ فحاول ار يجعل قيدا الا يه تفريع على التسوية ب حالا عنه - یہ متفرع ہے رعایة للام پر یعنی حال بنا کر دونوں کے اندر تن سب کو برت رار رکھا کہ یہ قیود ایک ہی جنس سے ہوں۔ الا انه قدمان
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praising Allah first and second, and the tongue of praise to Him second, and upon the best of His messengers Muhammad and his family, prayers and peace, in the arena of prayers, a state of being glorified and prayed upon. The word 'hamidan' is grammatically a hal from the pronoun that is hidden in 'bism' i.e., in the beginning it is hidden and concealed. The author says: 'I begin the book praising Allah'. He mentioned the object of 'begin' to indicate that the reality is that the bismillah is a lughw (redundant) clause connected to 'begin' and does not take the place of the object. Otherwise the meaning would be 'I begin the action with the book's beginning' without tasmiyah, while the intended meaning is second. Rather, in reality, the ba is related to 'tabarrukan' which carries the meaning of 'beginning'. The meaning is: I begin the book by blessing with the name of Allah. Similarly, 'hamidan' will be a hal from the pronoun in 'abtadi' and these two hals will be conditions for the beginning. The meaning is: I am beginning the book in the state of blessing with the name of Allah and praising Allah. This is the method of hal. That is, at this opening and beginning, the common method of the sentence would be to say 'I praise Allah', but the author abandoned that and adopted the method of hal because of the equalization between tahmid and tasmiyah so that there remains equality between them and the observance of proportionality is maintained. The intent of 'taswiyah' is that tahmid and tasmiyah both become conditions for the beginning and it becomes restricted by them. The intent of 'ri'ayat al-tanqish' is that the two conditions be of the same type: just as the bismillah becomes a hal by being connected to the hidden pronoun, similarly tahmid comes as a hal in the form of 'hamid'. Then the beginning becomes restricted by both restrictions. The objective is that these two restrictions are necessary for the beginning; without them, the beginning is not considered valid. For it has been narrated in a hadith... which urges equality between tasmiyah and tahmid. The intent is that since the hadith has declared both tasmiyah and tahmid necessary for the beginning of any action, the author adopted the hal construction and made them both conditions of the beginning in the form of hal. He tried to make them a restriction. This is a branch of observing proportionality, i.e., by making them hal, he maintained proportionality so that these restrictions are of the same type. However, they are old...
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening of a fiqh book (likely Al-Tawdih). The author explains why he used the word 'hamidan' (praising) as a hal clause instead of writing a separate sentence 'I praise Allah'. The reason is to create equality (taswiyah) between the tasmiyah (saying Bismillah) and the tahmid (praising), both of which are considered necessary conditions for starting any important act, as indicated in a hadith. By using the hal construction, both acts—blessing with Allah's name and praising Him—become simultaneous conditions of the same grammatical type, emphasizing their equal necessity. This reflects the author's methodological precision in aligning the form of expression with the legal principle that every significant action should begin with both tasmiyah and tahmid. The commentator elaborates on the grammatical analysis, showing how the hal clause relates to the hidden pronoun in 'bismillah' and to the verb 'abtadi' (I begin). This is a typical usul al-fiqh analysis of textual composition, demonstrating how linguistic choices can underscore legal maxims.

Key Terms
حال (hal): An Arabic grammatical term for a circumstantial clause describing the state of the subject or object at the time of the action.
تسمیہ (tasmiyah): The act of saying 'Bismillah' (in the name of Allah) at the start of an action.
تحمید (tahmid): The act of praising Allah, often by saying 'Alhamdulillah'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the author use 'hamidan' (a hal clause) instead of 'ahmadullah' (a separate sentence) in the opening?
A) To make the sentence grammatically simpler.
B) To create equality between tasmiyah and tahmid as conditions of the beginning.
C) Because the hadith requires it in that exact form.
D) To avoid ambiguity in the pronoun reference.

Key Takeaway
The hal construction 'hamidan' was deliberately chosen to equate tasmiyah and tahmid as simultaneous conditions for beginning, reflecting a hadith-based legal principle.

Method of Learning

The Author's Purpose and Methodological Principles
Author's statement of purpose and methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author's purpose in writing the sharh and state the methodological principles he adopts.

Core Idea
A good commentary clarifies difficulties while avoiding unnecessary verbosity, and relies on logical rules, not just objectives.

In this front matter passage, the author of the Tawdih explains why he wrote his commentary on Tanqih al-Usul and how he approached the task. He emphasizes that he will only explain what is difficult, not what is self-evident, and that his work is grounded in the logical rules of Mizan and Mantiq. Understanding this purpose helps us appreciate the structure and focus of the commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's stated purpose
Read the opening lines where the author says he intends to explain difficulties and clarify ambiguities, but will avoid points that are already clear.
This selective approach is key: the commentary is not exhaustive but targeted.
2
Recognize the scope of the commentary
Note that the author explicitly warns that anyone who cannot understand the clear points should not read his book. This defines the audience as advanced scholars.
This is a common feature of advanced Hanafi usul works.
3
Understand the revision process
The author describes how after the draft was copied, he made a second review and introduced changes. He then wrote the commentary based on the corrected text.
This ensures that the commentary aligns with the final version of Tanqih al-Usul.
4
Identify the methodological foundation
The author states that his arguments are founded on the science of Mizan and Mantiq (logic), unlike the earlier method that only explained objectives.
This reflects the Hanafi commitment to rigorous logical reasoning in usul.
5
Note the arrangement and style
The author describes his arrangement as 'elegant' and points to his modifications in advancing or delaying topics in the best manner.
This shows attention to pedagogical sequencing.

قال المصنف بتاليف تنقيح الاصول یہاں سے مصنف توضیح کی وجہ تصنیف پیش کر رہا ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے تنقیح الاصول کے تالیف کی توفیق عطا فرمائی تو میرا ارادہ ہوا کہ اس کے مشکلات کی تشریح کروں اور مغلقات کی توضیح اور تنقیح کے ان مقامات کے حل کرنے سے اعراض کروں گا کہ جن کا حل کرنا بجز اطناب کے اور کچھ نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ وہ مقام خود واضح ہیں اور جو شخص ایسے مقامات کو بھی نہیں سمجھ سکتا بلکہ اطناب کا محتاج ہے تو ایسے شخص کو میری اس کتاب میں نظر کہنا حلال نہیں ہے۔ واعلم اني لما سورت تفصیل کرتے ہوئے فرما رہے ہیں کہ جب میں نے اپنی کتاب تنفتح الاصول‎ کا مسودہ تیار کر لیا تو بہت سے اصحاب نے جلدی سے اس کا انتساخ یعنی نقل کر کے بحث و تبجیت شروع کر دی اس کے بعد نظر ثانی مصنف نے کی تو عبارت کے اندر خود مصنف کی جانب سے کچھ تغیرات اور محمود اثبات واقع ہوا جس کو مصنف نے ثمر بعد ذلك وقع فيه قليل من التغييرات وشى من المحو الاثبات کے ساتھ خود بیان فرمایا ہے فکتبت تو اس شرح میں متن تنقیح کی عبادت اس طریقہ پر لکھی جو نظر ثانی کی بعد متقرر اور ثابت ہوئے تاکہ سابقہ نسخ مکتوبہ کو بھی اس نمط و طریق کی طرف تبدیل کیا جائے ۔ تو لما تيسر اتمامه وفض بالاختتام ختامہ شارح علامہ نے اس کی تشریح کرتے ہوئے کہا فض من فضت ان ای فتحتہ اصل میں فض کا معنی ہوتا ہے کسی شی کو توڑ کر ٹکڑے ٹکڑے کرنا اختتام سے مراد ہے اختتمت الكتاب یعنی بلغت آخرہ اور ختام اسی مٹی اور لاک کا نام ہے جس پر مہر ثبت کر کے ایک شی کو سر بمہر کیا جاتا ہے چونکہ کتاب قبل از تمامیت لوگوں کی نظر سے محتجب اور مستور تھی تو یہ بمنزلہ شی مختوم کے تھی جس کے مخزونات اور مستودعات پر نہ اطلاع حاصل ہو سکتی ہے اور نہ احاطہ اور بعد الاختتام جب طالبین کے سامنے پیش ہوئی اور ان کو مطالعہ کا موقعہ دیا گیا تو گویا اس کی ختام توڑ دی گئی اور لوگوں کے سامنے ظاہر کر دی گئی۔ قوله مؤ سسة على قواعد اتم یعنی اس کتاب میں جو حج اور براہین پیش کئے گئے ہیں ان کی تاسیس و بنیاد ان وجوہ و شرائط پر ہے جو علم المیزان والمنطق میں مذکور ہیں اور اس کتاب میں طریق قدماء کو اختیار نہیں کیا گیا جو صرف تبیین مقاصد پر اکتفا کر لیتے تھے اور شرائط و ضوابط منطقیہ کی طرف زیادہ توجہ نہیں کرتے تھے۔ ترتیب انیق ای حسن معجب یعنی میری اس کتاب میں ترتیب مضامین بہت احسن اور پسندیدہ طریق پر ہے اس کے ساتھ اشارہ کر رہا ہے ان تصرفات کی طرف جو بعض مبات اور ابواب میں تقدیم و تاخیر کی ہے علی الوجه الاحسن - لويسبقني على مثله قال الشارح والصواب لم يسبقنی الی مثلہ یعنی صلہ الیٰ ہونا صواب ہے اور علی غلط ہے اس پر سبقت العالمین الی المعالی سے استشہاد کیا ۔ حالانکہ یہ محمول علی التضمین ہو سکتا ہے۔ تقدیر عبارت یوں ہو گی لم يسبقنی واقفا على مثلر و بار التضمين واسع عند العرب اور جو شعر استشہارا پیش کیا ہے عمر الخیام کا ہے جو مولدین سے ہے جن کی کلام لغت کے بارہ میں حجت نہیں ہو سکتی علاوہ ازیں سبقت بمعنی غلبہ متعدی بعلیٰ ہوا کرتی ہے جیسے قرآن مجید میں ہے وَمَا نحن مسبوقين على ان نبدل امثالكم معنیٰ ہو گا لم يغلبنی علی مثلہ احد و عدم کون المعنى ہنا علی ہذا ممنوع ۔ یہاں توضیح میں لفظ الهرمان واقع ہے جس کا معنیٰ کتب نعت میں العقل والرأی آتا ہے واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔ الى هذا الامد یا تو اس سے مراد ہے الی ہذہ الغایت من الزمان یعنی مصنف کے وقت و زمان تک فرسان علم ان تدقیقات تک نہیں پہنچ سکے ۔ یا مراد الی ہذہ الغایت من التدقیق یعنی تدقیق کی اس حث
The author said: 'By composing Tanqih al-Usul.' From here the author of the Tawdih presents the reason for authorship, the summary of which is that Allah granted success in composing Tanqih al-Usul, so I intended to explain its difficulties and clarify its ambiguities, and I will avoid solving those points of Tanqih whose solution would be nothing but verbosity because those points are themselves clear. And the person who cannot understand even such points but needs verbosity, then such a person is not permitted to look into my book. 'And know that when I drafted...' elaborating: When I completed the draft of my book Tanqih al-Usul, many associates hastily copied it and began discussion and criticism. After that, I performed a second review, and in the text there occurred some changes and some deletions and additions by the author himself, which the author expressed with 'thumma ba'da dhalika waqa'a fihi qalilun min al-taghyirat wa shay'un min al-mahw wa al-ithbat'. So I wrote in this commentary the text of Tanqih in the manner that was settled and established after the second review, so that the previously written copies could also be changed to this style and method. 'Then when its completion was facilitated and it was opened at the conclusion' - the commentator explained: 'Fadda' from 'fadat' meaning 'I opened it'. Originally, 'fadd' means to break something into pieces. 'Ikhtitam' means 'I completed the book', i.e., reached its end. 'Khitam' is the name of the clay and lacquer with which a seal is affixed and a thing is sealed. Since the book was hidden and covered from people's sight before completion, it was like a sealed thing whose stored contents and deposits could neither be accessed nor encompassed. After completion, when it was presented to seekers and they were given opportunity to study, it was as if its seal was broken and it was revealed to people. 'His saying: 'established upon complete principles' - meaning the proofs and arguments presented in this book are founded upon those reasons and conditions mentioned in the science of Mizan and Mantiq (logic). And in this book, the method of the ancients is not adopted, who used to suffice with explaining objectives and did not pay much attention to logical conditions and rules. 'An elegant arrangement' - i.e., beautiful and pleasing; meaning the arrangement of topics in my book is very beautiful and praiseworthy. With this, he is pointing to those modifications he made in some chapters and sections by advancing or delaying in the best manner. 'Nor did anyone precede me upon its like' - the commentator said: the correct is 'lam yasbiqni ila mithlihi', meaning the preposition 'ila' is correct and 'ala' is wrong. He cited 'sabaqa al-'alamin ila al-ma'ali' as evidence, although it can be carried on tadmeen. The implied phrase would be 'lam yasbiqni waqifan 'ala mithli', and tadmeen is vast in Arabic. The verse he cited as evidence is by 'Umar al-Khayyam, who is among the modern poets whose speech cannot be accepted as evidence in language. Moreover, 'sabaqa' in the sense of 'ghalaba' is transitive with 'ala', as in the Quran: 'wa ma nahnu bi-masbuqin 'ala an nubaddila amthalakum' meaning 'lam yaghlibni 'ala mithli ahad'. The non-existence of the meaning here being this is prevented. Here, in the Tawdih, the word 'al-harman' occurs, whose meaning in books of description is 'al-aql wa al-ray'. And Allah knows best what is correct. 'Until this limit' - either meaning 'until this time' i.e., up to the author's time, the knights of knowledge did not reach such minute investigations; or meaning 'until this limit of minute investigation'.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage serves as a front matter, explaining the author's purpose and methodology in writing his commentary (sharh) on Tanqih al-Usul. The author states that after completing Tanqih, he intended to clarify its difficulties and ambiguities, but explicitly avoids discussing points that are already clear, as doing so would only lead to unnecessary verbosity. He even declares that anyone who cannot understand those clear points has no right to look into his book. The passage then describes the process of the work: after the draft was copied and discussed by others, the author made a second review and introduced changes (deletions and additions). He ensured that his commentary quoted the corrected text so that earlier copies could be aligned. The commentator elaborates on the phrase 'fadda bi al-ikhtitam', explaining that 'fadd' means breaking open the seal, metaphorically indicating that the book was made available after completion. The author also clarifies that his work is based on the logical rules of 'Mizan' and 'Mantiq', unlike earlier scholars who focused only on objectives. He praises his own arrangement as elegant. Finally, the passage includes a rebuttal against a criticism about the preposition 'ala' instead of 'ila' in the phrase 'lam yasbiqni 'ala mithlihi'. The commentator argues that it can be interpreted via tadmeen, and the evidence cited by the critic (from 'Umar al-Khayyam) is not valid since poetry of later poets (mawalid) is not authoritative for linguistic evidence. He also gives a Quranic example to show that 'sabaqa' with the meaning of 'ghalaba' takes 'ala'. The passage concludes with an explanation of the word 'al-harman' and the phrase 'ila hadha al-amad'.

Key Terms
تضمین (tadmeen): Implication where a word is used with its real meaning and a second meaning is implied by indicating a deleted verb through its object or connector.
قواعد اتم (qawa'id atamm): Complete principles based on the science of logic (Mizan and Mantiq).
مولدون (mawalidun): Later poets (e.g., 'Umar al-Khayyam) whose speech is not considered authoritative linguistic evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the author avoid discussing certain points of Tanqih al-Usul?
A) They are too difficult and require a separate book.
B) They are already clear, so explaining them would only be verbose.
C) He did not have time to cover everything.
D) He wanted to leave them for other commentators.

Key Takeaway
The author's commentary is selective, logically grounded in Mizan and Mantiq, and written for an advanced audience.

Linguistic Tools in Usul: Tadmeen and Authority of Poets
Defense of the author's wording via tadmeen and rejection of later poetic evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the concept of tadmeen to defend a contested phrasing and evaluate the authority of later poets in linguistic evidence.

Core Idea
Tadmeen allows a valid alternate reading; later poets are not evidence for Arabic rules.

In a brief but significant passage, the commentator defends the author's phrase 'lam yasbiqni 'ala mithlihi' against a grammatical criticism. The defense uses the concept of tadmeen (implication) and a Quranic verse to show that the preposition 'ala' is acceptable. It also dismisses the critic's evidence from a later poet, arguing that such poets are not authoritative. This lesson dissects that linguistic argument, which is crucial for understanding how Hanafi usul scholars validate textual readings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested phrase and the criticism
The author wrote: 'lam yasbiqni 'ala mithlihi'. The commentator reports that some say the correct preposition is 'ila' (to), not 'ala' (upon), and that 'ala' is wrong.
This is a grammatical criticism based on usual usage of 'sabaqa'.
2
Understand the tadmeen response
The commentator argues that the phrase can be interpreted via tadmeen: the verb 'yasbiqni' implies a preceding verb like 'waqifan' (pausing), so the meaning is 'he did not precede me, pausing upon its like'. This makes 'ala' correct.
Tadmeen is a widely accepted linguistic device in Arabic.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
The commentator cites Quran 56:60: 'wa ma nahnu bi-masbuqin 'ala an nubaddila amthalakum' where 'sabaqa' is used with 'ala' meaning 'overcome'. This shows that 'sabaqa' with 'ala' is valid when meaning 'ghalaba'.
The verse is used as evidence that the construction is acceptable.
4
Evaluate the authority of the poet's evidence
The critic cited a line by 'Umar al-Khayyam as evidence for using 'ila'. The commentator rejects this because al-Khayyam is a later poet (mawalid), and his speech is not authoritative for linguistic rules.
Hanafi usul only accepts pre-Islamic and early Islamic poetry as evidence.
5
Conclude the defense
The commentator's response shows that the author's wording is correct either via tadmeen or by taking 'sabaqa' to mean 'ghalaba'. The criticism is baseless.
This is the final position: the phrase stands as written.

ہونا صواب ہے اور علی غلط ہے اس پر سبقت العالمین الی المعالی سے استشہاد کیا ۔ حالانکہ یہ محمول علی التضمین ہو سکتا ہے۔ تقدیر عبارت یوں ہو گی لم يسبقنی واقفا على مثلر و بار التضمين واسع عند العرب اور جو شعر استشہارا پیش کیا ہے عمر الخیام کا ہے جو مولدین سے ہے جن کی کلام لغت کے بارہ میں حجت نہیں ہو سکتی علاوہ ازیں سبقت بمعنی غلبہ متعدی بعلیٰ ہوا کرتی ہے جیسے قرآن مجید میں ہے وَمَا نحن مسبوقين على ان نبدل امثالكم معنیٰ ہو گا لم يغلبنی علی مثلہ احد و عدم کون المعنى ہنا علی ہذا ممنوع ۔ یہاں توضیح میں لفظ الهرمان واقع ہے جس کا معنیٰ کتب نعت میں العقل والرأی آتا ہے واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔ الى هذا الامد یا تو اس سے مراد ہے الی ہذہ الغایت من الزمان یعنی مصنف کے وقت و زمان تک فرسان علم ان تدقیقات تک نہیں پہنچ سکے ۔ یا مراد الی ہذہ الغایت من التدقیق یعنی تدقیق کی اس حث
The author said: 'By composing Tanqih al-Usul.' From here the author of the Tawdih presents the reason for authorship, the summary of which is that Allah granted success in composing Tanqih al-Usul, so I intended to explain its difficulties and clarify its ambiguities, and I will avoid solving those points of Tanqih whose solution would be nothing but verbosity because those points are themselves clear. And the person who cannot understand even such points but needs verbosity, then such a person is not permitted to look into my book. 'And know that when I drafted...' elaborating: When I completed the draft of my book Tanqih al-Usul, many associates hastily copied it and began discussion and criticism. After that, I performed a second review, and in the text there occurred some changes and some deletions and additions by the author himself, which the author expressed with 'thumma ba'da dhalika waqa'a fihi qalilun min al-taghyirat wa shay'un min al-mahw wa al-ithbat'. So I wrote in this commentary the text of Tanqih in the manner that was settled and established after the second review, so that the previously written copies could also be changed to this style and method. 'Then when its completion was facilitated and it was opened at the conclusion' - the commentator explained: 'Fadda' from 'fadat' meaning 'I opened it'. Originally, 'fadd' means to break something into pieces. 'Ikhtitam' means 'I completed the book', i.e., reached its end. 'Khitam' is the name of the clay and lacquer with which a seal is affixed and a thing is sealed. Since the book was hidden and covered from people's sight before completion, it was like a sealed thing whose stored contents and deposits could neither be accessed nor encompassed. After completion, when it was presented to seekers and they were given opportunity to study, it was as if its seal was broken and it was revealed to people. 'His saying: 'established upon complete principles' - meaning the proofs and arguments presented in this book are founded upon those reasons and conditions mentioned in the science of Mizan and Mantiq (logic). And in this book, the method of the ancients is not adopted, who used to suffice with explaining objectives and did not pay much attention to logical conditions and rules. 'An elegant arrangement' - i.e., beautiful and pleasing; meaning the arrangement of topics in my book is very beautiful and praiseworthy. With this, he is pointing to those modifications he made in some chapters and sections by advancing or delaying in the best manner. 'Nor did anyone precede me upon its like' - the commentator said: the correct is 'lam yasbiqni ila mithlihi', meaning the preposition 'ila' is correct and 'ala' is wrong. He cited 'sabaqa al-'alamin ila al-ma'ali' as evidence, although it can be carried on tadmeen. The implied phrase would be 'lam yasbiqni waqifan 'ala mithli', and tadmeen is vast in Arabic. The verse he cited as evidence is by 'Umar al-Khayyam, who is among the modern poets whose speech cannot be accepted as evidence in language. Moreover, 'sabaqa' in the sense of 'ghalaba' is transitive with 'ala', as in the Quran: 'wa ma nahnu bi-masbuqin 'ala an nubaddila amthalakum' meaning 'lam yaghlibni 'ala mithli ahad'. The non-existence of the meaning here being this is prevented. Here, in the Tawdih, the word 'al-harman' occurs, whose meaning in books of description is 'al-aql wa al-ray'. And Allah knows best what is correct. 'Until this limit' - either meaning 'until this time' i.e., up to the author's time, the knights of knowledge did not reach such minute investigations; or meaning 'until this limit of minute investigation'.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage serves as a front matter, explaining the author's purpose and methodology in writing his commentary (sharh) on Tanqih al-Usul. The author states that after completing Tanqih, he intended to clarify its difficulties and ambiguities, but explicitly avoids discussing points that are already clear, as doing so would only lead to unnecessary verbosity. He even declares that anyone who cannot understand those clear points has no right to look into his book. The passage then describes the process of the work: after the draft was copied and discussed by others, the author made a second review and introduced changes (deletions and additions). He ensured that his commentary quoted the corrected text so that earlier copies could be aligned. The commentator elaborates on the phrase 'fadda bi al-ikhtitam', explaining that 'fadd' means breaking open the seal, metaphorically indicating that the book was made available after completion. The author also clarifies that his work is based on the logical rules of 'Mizan' and 'Mantiq', unlike earlier scholars who focused only on objectives. He praises his own arrangement as elegant. Finally, the passage includes a rebuttal against a criticism about the preposition 'ala' instead of 'ila' in the phrase 'lam yasbiqni 'ala mithlihi'. The commentator argues that it can be interpreted via tadmeen, and the evidence cited by the critic (from 'Umar al-Khayyam) is not valid since poetry of later poets (mawalid) is not authoritative for linguistic evidence. He also gives a Quranic example to show that 'sabaqa' with the meaning of 'ghalaba' takes 'ala'. The passage concludes with an explanation of the word 'al-harman' and the phrase 'ila hadha al-amad'.

Key Terms
تضمین (tadmeen): Implication where a word is used with its real meaning and a second meaning is implied by indicating a deleted verb through its object or connector.
قواعد اتم (qawa'id atamm): Complete principles based on the science of logic (Mizan and Mantiq).
مولدون (mawalidun): Later poets (e.g., 'Umar al-Khayyam) whose speech is not considered authoritative linguistic evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the poetry of 'Umar al-Khayyam not accepted as evidence for Arabic linguistic rules in this passage?
A) Because he was not a native Arabic speaker.
B) Because he is a later poet (mawalid), whose speech is not authoritative.
C) Because the line does not have a clear chain of transmission.
D) Because the verse is about a different topic.

Key Takeaway
Tadmeen and alternative meanings can defend unusual constructions, and only early poetry is accepted as linguistic evidence.

The Classification of Sharia: Usul and Furu'
Explaining the classification of Sharia into foundational principles and derived branches, and the roles of Fiqh and Usul al-Fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define usul al-shari'ah and furu' al-shari'ah and explain their relationship using Hanafi terminology.

Core Idea
Usul are general proofs; Furu' are detailed rulings derived from them.

This passage from the sharh of Al-Taozeeh wa Al-Talweeh establishes the foundational classification of Sharia into principles (usul) and branches (furu'). Understanding this distinction is essential for navigating the Hanafi legal system and recognizing how rulings are derived from primary sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two components
Read the passage and locate where 'usul al-shari'ah' and 'furu' al-shari'ah' are mentioned. The author defines them as general proofs and detailed rulings respectively.
The terms are in Arabic: أصول الشريعة and فروع الشريعة.
2
Define usul al-shari'ah
Note that usul are the general proofs: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas. They are the foundational sources from which rulings are derived.
Hanafi usul considers these four as the primary sources.
3
Define furu' al-shari'ah
Furu' are the detailed rulings (ahkam tafsiliyyah) that are explained in fiqh. They are derived from the usul.
Furu' are the practical rules governing actions.
4
Understand the relationship
The author explains that furu' depend on usul: knowledge of detailed rulings requires knowledge of the general proofs. Also, the addition of 'furu'' to 'shari'ah' is an addition of part to whole, while 'usul' is addition of proof to proven.
This shows the interdependence.
5
Recognize the scope of Sharia
Sharia is broader than fiqh; it includes fiqh and usul issues like the vision of Allah and authority of ijma/ qiyas. This is important for understanding the hierarchy of sciences.
This subtlety is often missed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله على ان جعل تعليق یعنی مصنف نے محامد کو معلق اور وابستہ کر دیا ہے اس امر کے ساتھ کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے اصول شریعیت کو مہدۃ المبانی اور فروع شریعت کو رقیقہ الاطرف و دقیقہ المعانی کر دیا اور اللہ تعالیٰ کی نعمتوں میں سے یہ بعض نعمتیں نہیں حالانکہ محامد جمع مستغرق ہے جو جمیع انعامات کے ساتھ معلق اور وابستہ ہونی چاہیئے تھی تو بعض نعیم کی تخصیص کیوں کی شارح نے اس کی وجہ پیش کرتے ہوئے کہا اشارة الى عظما مر العلم یعنی یہ نعمت علمیہ کی تخصیص ہے اس کے ساتھ اس علم کی عظمت شان اور حلالہ قدر کی طرف اشارہ کر نا مطلوب ہے جس میں یہ تصنیف واقع ہے۔ والشريعة تعمر الفقہ یعنی شریعت سے مراد عمومی معنیٰ ہے جو فقہ کو بھی شامل ہے اور انہیں کے علاوہ ان اصولی مسائل کو بھی جو ادلہ سمعیہ سے ثابت ہیں جیسے مسئلہ رویہ باری تعالیٰ اور معاد و اجماع وقیاس کا حجت ہونا۔ اور اصول الشریعت سے مراد ادلہ کلیہ ہیں یعنی کتاب الله سنت رسول علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام اجماع و قیاس اور ان کے مبانی علم التوحید والصفات والنبوات ہیں یعنی علم الکلام جوان امور سے بحث کرتا ہے چونکہ کتاب و سنت کا اثبات ان مسائل کلامیہ پر موقوف ہے اس لئے یہ مسائل اصول فقہ کے لئے مبنی نہیں تمهیدھا کا معنی ہے تویہ اور ان کی اصلاح علی وفق الحق یعنی اللہ تعالیٰ نے اصول شریعیت کا تسویہ کر دیا اور علی طریقہ الصواب اور حق کے موافق ان کی وضع اور اصلاح فرمائی یہ ہے مراد از تمہید مبانی وفروعها ای فروع الشریعہ اس سے مراد احکام تفصلیہ جو علم الفقہ میں بیان کئے گئے۔ یعنی مسائل فقیہ چونکہ شریعت سے عمومی معنی مراد لیا گیا ہے جو فقہ کو بھی شامل تھا اس لئے فروعها ای فروع المشریعت میں اضافت فروع الی الشریعت اضافة الجزر الی الکل ہوگی اور اضافہ الاصول الی الشریعۃ اضافة الدليل الى المدلول ہوگی۔ دقيقة المعانی میں معانی سے مراد علل جزئیہ تفصیلیہ ہیں جو علم الفقہ میں ہر مسئلہ پر پیش کی جاتی ہیں اور وہ علل دقیقہ ہیں ہر ایک انسان ان تک بالسہولت نہیں پہنچ سکتا بلکہ ان کا استخراج مجتہد کا کام ہے اور یہ تمام اشیاء اللہ تعالیٰ کی طرف سے نعمتیں ہیں جو کہ مستوجب محمد ہیں کیونکہ شریعت ایک ایسی نعمت ہے جس کے ساتھ نظام عالم قائم اور صحیح رہتا ہے اور عالم آخرہ میں ثواب کی دارو مدار اسی پر ہے اور رقت معانی کی وجہ سے علماء کے درجات رفیع ہوتے ہیں اور اللہ تعالیٰ کے ہاں انہیں حصولِ ثواب ہو گا اس کلام سے معلوم ہوا کہ علم الاصول علم الفقہ سے فوقانی درجہ رکھتا ہے کیونکہ احکام جزئیہ فقہیہ کی معرفت از ادلہ تفصیلیہ جو مسائل فقہ ہیں یہ ادلہ کلیہ کے احوال کی معرفت پر موقوف ہیں جن سے علم الاصول بحث کرتا ہے اور یہ علم الاصول چونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ اور اس کی صفات کی معرفت پر اور اسی طرح صدق مبلغ بدلالتہ المعجزات کی معرفت پر موقوف ہے جن سے علم الکلام بحث کرتا ہے ۔ لہذا علم الکلام کی بنسبت اسے درجہ سختانی حاصل ہے
His statement 'ala anna ja'ala ta'liq' means the author made the praises (mahamid) dependent and attached to this matter: that Allah made the principles of Sharia (usul al-shari'ah) well-laid foundations and the branches of Sharia (furu' al-shari'ah) subtle in their aspects and precise in their meanings. And these are not some of the blessings of Allah, whereas 'mahamid' is an inclusive plural that should be attached to all blessings. So why specify some blessings? The commentator (sharih) advanced the reason, saying: it is an indication of the greatness of the status of knowledge (al-ilm) — i.e., it is a specification of the blessing of knowledge, to indicate the majesty and high value of this knowledge in which this composition lies. And 'al-shari'ah ta'muru al-fiqh' means that by 'shari'ah' is intended a general meaning that includes fiqh and, besides them, those usul issues that are established by revealed evidence (adillah sam'iyyah), such as the issue of the vision of Allah, the resurrection, and the authority of ijma and qiyas. And by 'usul al-shari'ah' is meant general proofs (adillah kulliyyah) i.e., the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger, ijma, and qiyas; and their foundations are the sciences of tawhid, attributes, and prophethood — i.e., the science of kalam (theology), which discusses these matters. Since the proof of the Book and Sunnah depends on these theological issues, these issues are foundations (mabani) for usul al-fiqh. 'Tamhiduha' means their rectification and correction in accordance with the truth — i.e., Allah rectified the principles of Sharia and set them in the correct way and in conformity with truth; this is the meaning of 'tamhid al-mabani.' And 'furu'uha' i.e., the branches of Sharia; by them is meant detailed rulings (ahkam tafsiliyyah) which are explained in the science of fiqh. Since 'shari'ah' is taken in a general sense that includes fiqh, therefore the addition of 'furu'' to 'shari'ah' is an addition of a part to the whole. And the addition of 'usul' to 'shari'ah' is an addition of the proof to the proven (dalil ila madlul). In 'daiqa al-ma'ani', by 'ma'ani' is meant detailed partial causes (ilal juz'iyyah tafsiliyyah) that are presented in fiqh for every issue, and those causes are precise; not every person can easily reach them, rather their extraction is the work of a mujtahid. And all these things are blessings from Allah that merit praise, because Sharia is a blessing through which the order of the world is established and remains correct, and in the afterlife reward depends on it. And because of the subtlety of meanings, the ranks of scholars are elevated and they attain reward with Allah. From this speech it is understood that the science of usul (usul al-fiqh) holds a superior rank over the science of fiqh, because the knowledge of detailed fiqh rulings from detailed proofs (which are the issues of fiqh itself) depends on knowledge of the conditions of general proofs (adillah kulliyyah), which the science of usul discusses. And this science of usul, since it depends on knowledge of Allah and His attributes and similarly on the truthfulness of the messenger through miracles (mu'jizat), which the science of kalam discusses, therefore in relation to kalam it holds a lower rank (darajah thaniyyah? but the text says 'sakhtani' which might be a typo).
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage clarifies the hierarchical structure of Islamic sciences as understood in the Hanafi usul tradition. The author explains that the praises (محامد) have been attached specifically to the scientific blessings that led to this work, highlighting the significance of usul al-fiqh. He then defines key terms: شریعت (Sharia) here is broad, encompassing both fiqh (detailed rulings) and usul issues like the vision of Allah, resurrection, and the authority of ijma and qiyas. اصول الشریعت (usul al-shari'ah) refers to the four general proofs: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. These prove the detailed rulings. The مبانی (foundations) of these usul are the theological sciences (tawhid, attributes, prophethood, etc.) studied in علم الکلام (theology), because the authority of Quran and Sunnah depends on proving prophethood and the existence of God. Thus, usul al-fiqh depends on kalam for its foundations. The text then distinguishes between the addition (اضافت) of branches and principles to Sharia: branches are part of Sharia (جزء to کل), while principles are the evidence (دلیل) for the rulings (مدلول). The precise meanings (دقیقہ المعانی) refer to the detailed legal causes (علل جزئیہ) that only a mujtahid can identify. The passage concludes that usul al-fiqh is superior to fiqh because it deals with the general proofs that detail rulings depend on, but it is inferior to kalam, which provides the foundations for usul al-fiqh. This hierarchical view is characteristic of the Hanafi school, emphasizing the interdependence of jurisprudence and theology.

Key Terms
أصول الشريعة (usul al-shari'ah): The general proofs (ادله کلیہ) of Sharia: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas.
فروع الشريعة (furu' al-shari'ah): The detailed rulings (احکام تفصیلیہ) derived from the proofs, which are the subject of Fiqh.
علل جزئیہ (ilal juz'iyyah): The specific legal causes behind individual rulings, which are precise and require ijtihad to extract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does 'al-shari'ah ta'muru al-fiqh' mean?
A) Sharia is limited to fiqh.
B) Sharia includes fiqh and also usul issues established by revealed evidence.
C) Sharia and fiqh are identical.
D) Fiqh is broader than Sharia.

Key Takeaway
Sharia is composed of general proofs (usul) and detailed rulings (furu'), and the knowledge of usul is necessary for deriving furu'.

Method of Learning
intermediate
10 min
The Hierarchy of Islamic Sciences: Fiqh, Usul, and Kalam
Explaining the classification of Sharia into foundational principles and derived branches, and the roles of Fiqh and Usul al-Fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the hierarchical relationship between Fiqh, Usul al-Fiqh, and Kalam according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh is superior to Fiqh but inferior to Kalam.

The passage not only defines usul and furu' but also establishes a clear hierarchy among the Islamic sciences. This lesson focuses on the ranking: Fiqh depends on Usul al-Fiqh, and Usul al-Fiqh depends on Kalam. Understanding this hierarchy is crucial for appreciating the Hanafi approach to legal theory and the curriculum.

Guided Path
1
Locate the hierarchy statements
Find in the passage the sentence that states 'علم الاصول علم الفقہ سے فوقانی درجہ رکھتا ہے' and the later reference to kalam giving it a lower rank.
These are explicit statements of superiority and inferiority.
2
Understand why usul is superior to fiqh
The passage explains that knowledge of detailed fiqh rulings depends on knowledge of the general proofs (adillah kulliyyah), which usul discusses. Thus, usul provides the foundation for fiqh.
This is a logical dependence.
3
Understand why kalam is superior to usul
Usul al-fiqh depends on kalam because proving the authority of the Quran and Sunnah requires knowledge of tawhid, prophethood, and miracles. Kalam establishes these foundations.
Without kalam, the proofs of usul would lack grounding.
4
Apply the hierarchy to the curriculum
In the traditional Hanafi curriculum, students typically study kalam first, then usul al-fiqh, then fiqh. This order reflects the dependency.
This practical sequence is derived from the conceptual hierarchy.
5
Recognize the broader implication
The hierarchy shows that Islamic legal theory is not isolated but embedded within a broader theological framework. This ensures that legal rulings are rooted in correct belief.
This is a distinctive feature of the Hanafi approach.

رسول علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام اجماع و قیاس اور ان کے مبانی علم التوحید والصفات والنبوات ہیں یعنی علم الکلام جوان امور سے بحث کرتا ہے چونکہ کتاب و سنت کا اثبات ان مسائل کلامیہ پر موقوف ہے اس لئے یہ مسائل اصول فقہ کے لئے مبنی نہیں تمهیدھا کا معنی ہے تویہ اور ان کی اصلاح علی وفق الحق یعنی اللہ تعالیٰ نے اصول شریعیت کا تسویہ کر دیا اور علی طریقہ الصواب اور حق کے موافق ان کی وضع اور اصلاح فرمائی یہ ہے مراد از تمہید مبانی وفروعها ای فروع الشریعہ اس سے مراد احکام تفصلیہ جو علم الفقہ میں بیان کئے گئے۔ یعنی مسائل فقیہ چونکہ شریعت سے عمومی معنی مراد لیا گیا ہے جو فقہ کو بھی شامل تھا اس لئے فروعها ای فروع المشریعت میں اضافت فروع الی الشریعت اضافة الجزر الی الکل ہوگی اور اضافہ الاصول الی الشریعۃ اضافة الدليل الى المدلول ہوگی۔ دقيقة المعانی میں معانی سے مراد علل جزئیہ تفصیلیہ ہیں جو علم الفقہ میں ہر کیونکہ شریعت ایک ایسی نعمت ہے جس کے ساتھ نظام عالم قائم اور صحیح رہتا ہے اور عالم آخرہ میں ثواب کی دارو مدار اسی پر ہے اور رقت معانی کی وجہ سے علماء کے درجات رفیع ہوتے ہیں اور اللہ تعالیٰ کے ہاں انہیں حصولِ ثواب ہو گا اس کلام سے معلوم ہوا کہ علم الاصول علم الفقہ سے فوقانی درجہ رکھتا ہے کیونکہ احکام جزئیہ فقہیہ کی معرفت از ادلہ تفصیلیہ جو مسائل فقہ ہیں یہ ادلہ کلیہ کے احوال کی معرفت پر موقوف ہیں جن سے علم الاصول بحث کرتا ہے اور یہ علم الاصول چونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ اور اس کی صفات کی معرفت پر اور اسی طرح صدق مبلغ بدلالتہ المعجزات کی معرفت پر موقوف ہے جن سے علم الکلام بحث کرتا ہے ۔ لہذا علم الکلام کی بنسبت اسے درجہ سختانی حاصل ہے
His statement 'ala anna ja'ala ta'liq' means the author made the praises (mahamid) dependent and attached to this matter: that Allah made the principles of Sharia (usul al-shari'ah) well-laid foundations and the branches of Sharia (furu' al-shari'ah) subtle in their aspects and precise in their meanings. And these are not some of the blessings of Allah, whereas 'mahamid' is an inclusive plural that should be attached to all blessings. So why specify some blessings? The commentator (sharih) advanced the reason, saying: it is an indication of the greatness of the status of knowledge (al-ilm) — i.e., it is a specification of the blessing of knowledge, to indicate the majesty and high value of this knowledge in which this composition lies. And 'al-shari'ah ta'muru al-fiqh' means that by 'shari'ah' is intended a general meaning that includes fiqh and, besides them, those usul issues that are established by revealed evidence (adillah sam'iyyah), such as the issue of the vision of Allah, the resurrection, and the authority of ijma and qiyas. And by 'usul al-shari'ah' is meant general proofs (adillah kulliyyah) i.e., the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger, ijma, and qiyas; and their foundations are the sciences of tawhid, attributes, and prophethood — i.e., the science of kalam (theology), which discusses these matters. Since the proof of the Book and Sunnah depends on these theological issues, these issues are foundations (mabani) for usul al-fiqh. 'Tamhiduha' means their rectification and correction in accordance with the truth — i.e., Allah rectified the principles of Sharia and set them in the correct way and in conformity with truth; this is the meaning of 'tamhid al-mabani.' And 'furu'uha' i.e., the branches of Sharia; by them is meant detailed rulings (ahkam tafsiliyyah) which are explained in the science of fiqh. Since 'shari'ah' is taken in a general sense that includes fiqh, therefore the addition of 'furu'' to 'shari'ah' is an addition of a part to the whole. And the addition of 'usul' to 'shari'ah' is an addition of the proof to the proven (dalil ila madlul). In 'daiqa al-ma'ani', by 'ma'ani' is meant detailed partial causes (ilal juz'iyyah tafsiliyyah) that are presented in fiqh for every issue, and those causes are precise; not every person can easily reach them, rather their extraction is the work of a mujtahid. And all these things are blessings from Allah that merit praise, because Sharia is a blessing through which the order of the world is established and remains correct, and in the afterlife reward depends on it. And because of the subtlety of meanings, the ranks of scholars are elevated and they attain reward with Allah. From this speech it is understood that the science of usul (usul al-fiqh) holds a superior rank over the science of fiqh, because the knowledge of detailed fiqh rulings from detailed proofs (which are the issues of fiqh itself) depends on knowledge of the conditions of general proofs (adillah kulliyyah), which the science of usul discusses. And this science of usul, since it depends on knowledge of Allah and His attributes and similarly on the truthfulness of the messenger through miracles (mu'jizat), which the science of kalam discusses, therefore in relation to kalam it holds a lower rank (darajah thaniyyah? but the text says 'sakhtani' which might be a typo).
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage clarifies the hierarchical structure of Islamic sciences as understood in the Hanafi usul tradition. Thus, usul al-fiqh depends on kalam for its foundations. Method of Learning
intermediate
6 min
Ordering of Idafi and Laqabi Definitions in Usul al-Fiqh
Explains why the idafi definition precedes the laqabi definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi author prioritizes the idafi definition over the laqabi definition and apply the principle of avoiding circularity in definitions.

Core Idea
Present the compound definition first to avoid repetition and maintain methodological soundness.

This passage discusses the proper order for defining the science of usul al-fiqh. The author chooses to define it first as a compound (idafi) and then as a title (laqabi). Some scholars prefer the opposite order. The author gives two clear reasons for his choice, focusing on the origin of the term and the need to avoid circular definitions. Understanding this ordering helps us appreciate the Hanafi method of defining technical terms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Definitions
Recognize that 'usul al-fiqh' can be defined as a compound (idafi) requiring definition of 'usul' and 'fiqh', or as a proper noun (laqabi) for the discipline itself. The author addresses both.
The idafi definition is analytical; the laqabi is synthetic.
2
Understand the Opposing View
Some scholars (like Ibn al-Hajib) present the laqabi definition first, arguing that the technical meaning is primary and simpler, like a simple precedes a compound.
This view values conciseness and directness.
3
Analyze the Author's First Reason
The compound construction (idafi) is the origin (manqūl ‘anhu) from which the laqab is derived. The origin has precedence over the derivative in a methodological discussion.
This is a logical priority: what is transferred from takes precedence.
4
Analyze the Author's Second Reason
If the laqabi definition comes first, then ‘fiqh’ must be defined in both definitions, causing useless repetition. The idafi-first order defines ‘fiqh’ once, and the laqabi definition can then refer to it without redundancy.
This avoids the error found in Ibn al-Hajib's work.
5
Observe the Pronoun Shift
The author uses feminine pronoun 'ha' for the idafi definition (as plural of non-rationals) and masculine 'hu' for the laqabi definition (as singular). This grammatical shift confirms the conceptual difference.
The shift is a subtle indicator of the two distinct meanings.

محکوم علیہ کے متعلق ہے۔ المقدمة یعنی اس کا مقدمہ اس علم کی تعریف اور تعیین موضوع کے بارہ میں ہے اور ان امور کی ضرورت اس لئے پیش آتی ہے کہ لان من حق الطالب یعنی جو شخص ایسی کثرہ کا طالب ہے جو ایک جہتر میں مضبوط اور ضبط شدہ ہے تو اس کے لئے لائق ہے کہ ان یعرفها معینی اولاً تو اس کی معرفت ضروری ہے کیونکہ جب تک مطلوب کی معرفت حاصل نہیں ہوگی تو وہ مجہول رہے گا اور مجہول مطلق کی طلب محال ہے بتلك الجهة مضبوطہ ہے اور اس کی جہت ضابطہ ایک تو اس علم کی تعریف ہوتی ہے جس کی وجہ سے وہ علم طالب علم کے نزدیک متمیز عن الاخیار ہو جاتا ہے دوسری تعیین موضوع جس کی بنیاد پر علم مطلوب فی نفسه وفي حد ذاته ممتاز عن سائر العلوم ہو جاتا ہے ۔ اس اصول فقہ کے طالب کا نفس اور قلب شوق مند ہو گا کہ اس فن کی تعریف معلوم ہو جائے تاکہ یہ علم اس کے نزدیک متمیز ہو جائے تو مصنف نے اشتیاق طالب کو پورا کرنے کی خاطر کہا لہذا الذی اذکرہ اصول الفقہ تا کہ سامع اور طالب کو سوال کرنے کی ضرورت پیش نہ آئے ۔ یا طالب علم کی لسان سے از خود سوال کر لیا کہ اصول الفقہ ماہی اس کے بعد تعریف شروع کردی۔ واصول الفقه لقب اصول الفقہ کے تعریفی حیثیت سے دو اعتبار ہیں ایک یہ کہ اس فن مخصوص کا لقب ہے جو مرکب اضافی سے منقول ہے اور مرکب اضافی اس کے لئے بدرجہ منقول عنہ ہے۔ فله بكل اعتبار تعریف یعنی با عتبار لقب ہونے کے الگ تعریف ہے اور باعتبار مرکب اضافی ہونے کے الگ قدم بعضهم یعنی بعض حضرات نے اس کی تعریف لقبی کو مقدم کیا کیونکہ اعلام میں معنی علمی مقصود بالذات ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس کو مقدم ہونا چاہیئے دوسری وجہ یہ کہ معنی علمی بنسبت معنی اضافی کے ایسے ہے جیسے مرتبہ بسیط بنسبت مرکب کے ہوتا ہے اور تقدیم بسیط علی المرکب زیادہ مناسب ہے۔ والمصنف قدم الاضافی لیکن مصنف نے اس کی تعریف اضافی کو مقدم کیا لو جہین ایک تو یہ کہ مرکب اضافی منقول عنہ ہے اور منقول عنہ کا رتبہ منقول الیہ پر مقدم ہوتا ہے ۔ دوسری وجہ یہ کہ تعریف لقبی میں لفظ الفقہ ماخوذ ہے جو مرکب اضافی میں مضاف الیہ ہے اگر اس کی تعریف لقبی معنی سے پہلے مذکور ہو جائے تو پھر اس کا ذکر تعریف یقینی میں صحیح ہو جائے گا جیسے مصنف نے آگے جا کہ اس کی تعریف لقبی میں کہا ہے ہو العلم بالقواعد التي يتوصل بہا الی الفقہ چونکہ مصنف پہلے تعریف اضافی میں فقہ کی تعریف ذکر کر چکا ہے لہذا لقبی میں اس کا ذکر صحیح ہے کیونکہ اس کی معرفت پہلے ہو چکی ہے اگر تعریف لقبی کو مقدم کیا جائے تو اس کے لئے تعریف فقہ کرنی ضروری ہو جائے گی ورنہ جہالت فی التعریف لازم آئے گی پھر تا نیا اس تعریف فقہ کا ذکر تعریف اضافی میں بھی ضروری ہے کیونکہ مرکب اضافی کی معرفت مضافین کلیہا کی معرفت پر موقوف ہے تو تعریف فقہ میں بے فائدہ تکرار آجائے گا جیسے کہ اصول ابن حاجب میں اس تکرار کا ارتکاب کیا گیا ہے کیونکہ انہوں نے تعریف لقبی کو مقدم کیا ہے ۔ ولما كان اصول الفقه مصنف نے تعریف اضافی کرتے ہوئے کہا فنعر فہا اولا بتانیث الضمیر اور لقبی کی تعریف میں فالآن تعرفہ ضمیر کو مذکر کیا یہ فرق کیوں ہے تو شارح نے اس کی وجہ پیش کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ معنی اضافی کے وقت میں یہ جمع ہے کیونکہ مجموعہ مضا فین کا معنی پیش کرنا ہے اور معنی لقبی کے لحاظ سے مفرد ہے جیسے عبداللہ علمی معنی کے لحاظ سے مفرد اور اضافی معنی کے لحاظ سے مرکب تو مصنف نے معنی انسانی میں اس کی جمعیت کی رعایت کی اور کہا تعرفہا ضمیر مؤنث لایا کیونکہ جمع غیر ذوی العقول کی طرف ضمیر مؤنث غائبہ کا راجع کیا جاتا ہے اور لقبی معنی چونکہ مفرد تھا اس لئے واحد مذکر کا ضمیر لایا اور کہا نصفه واللقب علم لقب ایسے علم کو کہتے ہیں جو اپنے معنی کے ساتھ مشعر بطرف مدح ہو یا ذم اصول الفقہ کا لفظ اپنے معنی کے لحاظ سے مشعر ہوئے مدح ہے کیونکہ یہ علم الفقہ جس کے ساتھ نظام معاش دنیا وی اور سنجات معاد یعنی اخروی حاصل ہوتی ہے یہ فن اس کی مبنی اور بنیاد ہے و ذلك مدح لہذا یہ لقب مادح ہوا ۔
It pertains to the one under ruling. The introduction is about the definition of this science and the determination of its subject. The need for these matters arises because it is the right of the student: whoever seeks such a multiplicity that is firmly and systematically organized in one aspect, then it is fitting for him to know it specifically first. His knowledge is necessary because as long as knowledge of what is sought is not obtained, it will remain unknown, and seeking the absolutely unknown is impossible. With that aspect, then it is necessary that he know what is sought from that aspect, so that he may be secure from missing the objective and from occupying himself with other than the objective. Matters that are connected and related to that aspect, he will understand that they are his sought objects and will strive to obtain them. Matters not related to that aspect, he will abandon them and not waste time seeking them. And every science is a well-organized multiplicity, and its organizing aspect is one: first, the definition of that science, through which the science is distinguished from others for the student; second, the determination of its subject, on which basis the science is distinguished in itself and in its essence from other sciences. The student of usul al-fiqh will have his soul and heart eager to know the definition of this art so that this science becomes distinguished for him. Therefore, the author said, in order to fulfill the student's eagerness: 'Therefore, what I mention is usul al-fiqh,' so that the listener and student have no need to ask. Or the student asked by tongue: 'What is usul al-fiqh?' after which he began the definition. And 'usul al-fiqh' as a title: the definition of usul al-fiqh has two aspects: one is that it is a title of this specific art, which is transferred from a compound construction, and the compound construction is the origin from which it is transferred. So it has a definition in each aspect: i.e., it has a separate definition as a title and a separate definition as a compound construction. Some scholars presented the title definition first, because among proper nouns, the technical meaning is intended essentially, so it should be presented. Second, the technical meaning in relation to the compound meaning is like the simple rank in relation to the compound, and presenting the simple before the compound is more appropriate. But the author presented the compound definition first, for two reasons: one, the compound construction is the origin from which it is transferred, and the origin has precedence over the derivative. Second, in the title definition, the word 'fiqh' is taken, which is the second part of the compound. If the title definition were mentioned first, then mentioning fiqh in the compound definition would be correct only after it had been defined. But since the author first mentions the compound definition, he defines fiqh there, and then in the title definition he says: 'It is knowledge of the rules by which one arrives at fiqh.' Because the author has already defined fiqh in the compound definition, so mentioning it in the title definition is correct because its knowledge has already been obtained. If the title definition were presented first, it would require defining fiqh then, otherwise ignorance in the definition would be necessary. Then later, mentioning this definition of fiqh in the compound definition would also be necessary because knowledge of the compound depends on knowledge of both parts together. So there would be useless repetition, as occurred in Usul Ibn al-Hajib because they presented the title definition first. And since 'usul al-fiqh' in the compound definition, the author said 'fa’rifha awwalan' using feminine pronoun, while in the title definition he said 'fa’l-’an ta’rifuhu' using masculine pronoun. What is the difference? The commentator explained that in the compound meaning, it is plural because it conveys the meaning of the sum of two parts, while in the title meaning it is singular, like 'Abdullah' is singular in technical meaning and compound in additive meaning. So the author, in the compound meaning, considered its plurality and used feminine pronoun because the plural of non-rational beings takes feminine singular pronoun. And in the title meaning, since it is singular, he used masculine singular pronoun. And he said: 'the title': a title is a name that indicates praise or blame with its meaning. The word 'usul al-fiqh' indicates praise because this science of fiqh, through which the system of worldly life and the salvation of the afterlife are attained, this art is its foundation and basis, and that is praise. Therefore, this title is praiseworthy.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage defines usul al-fiqh and discusses the proper order of its definitions. The author starts by explaining that every science needs a definition and a subject matter. The student must know what he is seeking. The author then presents the definition of usul al-fiqh in two ways: as a proper noun (laqab) and as a compound of 'usul' and 'fiqh' (idafi). Some scholars prefer the laqabi definition first because the technical meaning is primary. However, the author (al-Muṣannif) prefers the idafi definition first because it is the origin from which the laqab is derived, and it prevents repetition. The commentator (al-Shāriḥ) supports this, noting that the idafi definition allows defining 'fiqh' first, so that when the laqabi definition is given later (as 'knowledge of the rules leading to fiqh'), the term 'fiqh' is already understood. This avoids circularity and redundant definitions, a flaw seen in Ibn al-Hajib's arrangement. The passage also explains the grammatical difference in pronoun usage: feminine for the idafi meaning (as plural of non-rationals) and masculine for the laqabi meaning (as singular). Finally, it notes that 'usul al-fiqh' is a praiseworthy title because fiqh is the basis for worldly and religious welfare.

Key Terms
تعریف اضافی (ta'rīf iḍāfī): The definition of 'usul al-fiqh' as a compound construction (usul + fiqh), requiring definition of each part.
تعریف لقبی (ta'rīf laqabī): The definition of 'usul al-fiqh' as a proper noun/title for the discipline.
لقب (laqab): A title that implies praise or blame; here 'usul al-fiqh' is a praiseworthy title.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author (al-Muṣannif) present the idafi definition of usul al-fiqh before the laqabi definition?
A) Because the idafi definition is simpler and easier to understand.
B) Because the compound is the origin (manqūl ‘anhu) and presenting it first avoids repetition in defining fiqh.
C) Because the laqabi definition is not considered valid in Hanafi usul.
D) Because the author wanted to follow the order of Ibn al-Hajib.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi author prioritizes the idafi definition to establish the origin and prevent circular repetition in defining the science.

Method of Learning

8 min
Types of Definition: Haqiqi vs Ismi and the Order of Inquiry
Explains the two types of definition and the logical order of inquiry in Hanafi usul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between haqiqi and ismi definitions, apply the correct definition type based on the nature of the defined thing, and sequence the three instruments of inquiry (ma ismiyya, hal basita, ma haqiyya) in their proper order.

Core Idea
Definitions are real when they explain essence, nominal when they explain the name; inquiry proceeds from name to existence to essence.

This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh text lays the foundation for understanding how definitions work in Islamic legal theory. It distinguishes between two fundamental types of definition—haqiqi (real) and ismi (nominal)—and establishes a logical order for investigating any unknown concept. Mastering this distinction is essential for properly applying definitions in fiqh and for understanding how scholars analyze terms before deriving rulings.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish haqiqi and ismi definitions
Define both types: haqiqi explains the real essence (mahiyat haqiqiyya) using essential properties or accidents; ismi clarifies the meaning of the name using a more well-known term or elaboration. Identify which parts of the source text define each.
Haqiqi definitions answer 'what is it?' (ma haqiyya); ismi definitions answer 'what does the name mean?' (ma ismiyya).
2
Apply the rule to non-existents and existents
From the text: non-existents (ma'dumat) have no real essence, so only ismi definitions apply. Existents (mawjudat) can have both: ismi if only the concept is intended, haqiqi if the reality is sought. Apply this to a simple example like 'jinn'.
Non-existents like 'shirk' as a non-entity? Actually, shirk is existent as concept; better to use 'al-ihata' (circumference) for a non-existent? The text's example is not given, but the principle is clear.
3
Analyze the commentator's objection and resolution
The objector claims that the author's wording (definitions of real essences are haqiqi, conceptual ones are ismi) contradicts the allowance of ismi definitions for existents. Trace the three harmonizing responses: (a) qualification of perspective, (b) majority not universal, (c) illustrative not restrictive. Then see the final investigation (tahqiq) that resolves it by distinguishing between absolute essence and essence taken with mental consideration.
The final investigation introduces the three instruments of inquiry as the underlying reason for the distinction.
4
Sequence the three instruments of inquiry
From the text: The logical order is (1) ma ismiyya (explanation of the name), (2) hal basita (verification of existence), (3) ma haqiyya (inquiry into essence). State the purpose of each and why they must follow this order.
This order ensures that we are investigating something we can meaningfully define and that exists before seeking its essence.

واما اسمی کتعریف الما بميات الاعتبار یہ ۔ چونکہ ماہیات اعتباری کی تعریف صرف اسمی ہوتی ہے حقیقی نہیں ہوتی تو اس کا تقابل جو مصنف کی عبارت میں موجود ہے وہ تقاضا کرتا ہے کہ ماہیات حقیقیہ یعنی موجودہ و کی بحیثیت ماہیات حقیقیہ ہونے کے ہمیشہ حقیقی ہوتی ہے یا یوں کہا جائے کہ ماہیات کی تعریف فی الاکثر حقیقی ہوتی ہے لا علی سبیل الاطراد و الکلیہ یا یوں کہا جائے کہ مصنف کی عبادت محمول علی التمثیل ہے لا علی جواب بنتی ہے جو طلب حقیقت کے لئے موضوع ہے اور ما حقیقیہ کے جواب میں ہمیشہ تعریف حقیقی واقع ہوتی ہے اسمی نہیں ہو سکتی بلکہ تعریف اسمی ما شارجہ اور اسمیہ جس کی وضع شرح اسم اور بیان مفہوم کی طلب کے لئے کی گئی ہے جو کہ ما حقیقیہ سے دو درجے مقدم ہے اس کے جواب میں تعریف اسمی واقع ہوتی ہے۔ اِن مطالب یعنی آلات طلب میں اہل میزان کے نزدیک ترتیب یہ ہے چونکہ مجہول مطلق کی طلب نہیں ہو سکتی اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ مطلوب کا تصور بوجہ ما ذہن میں ہونا چاہیئے اس لئے مطلوب کی شرح اسم ضروری ہے ورنہ اس کی طلب نہیں ہو سکتی اور اس تصور اور شرح اسم کی طلب کے لئے ما شارحہ اسمیہ کی وضع کی گئی ہے جو تمام امہات المطالب سے مقدم ہے جب شرح اسم ہو جائے گی تو اس کی حقیقت کی طلب اور دریافت نہیں کی جاسکتی جب تک اس کے وجود فی نفسہ کی تصدیق نہ ہو جائے کیونکہ حقیقت اور ماہیت موجودات کی ہوتی ہے معدومات کی کوئی حقیقت ثابتہ نہیں ہوتی بلکہ ان کے صرف مفہومات ہوتے ہیں لہذا طلب حقیقت سے پہلے تصدیق بالوجود ضروری ہے اور اس تصدیق بالوجود فی نفسہ کی طلب کے لئے امہات المطالب میں سے ہل بسیطہ کی وضع کی گئی ہے تو حل بسیطہ ما شارحہ اسمیہ سے مؤخر ہوا اور ما حقیقیہ سے مقدم ہوا تصدیق بالوجود فی نفسہ کے حاصل ہو جانے کے بعد اب طلب حقیقت ہو سکتی ہے جس کے لئے ما حقیقیہ کی وضع ہے تو ما حقیقیہ کے جواب میں جو تعریف واقع ہوتی ہے وہ ہمیشہ تعریف حقیقی ہوتی ہے۔ وھی ای ما الحقيقية متاخرة عن هل البسيطة الطالبة لوجود الشئ المتأخرة یہ صفت ہے محل بسیطہ کی عن ما التي لطلب تفسير الاسم یہ وہی ما اسمیہ ہے جو حل بسیطہ سے مقدم ہے۔ وقدیر خذ من حيث انها مفهوم الاسم
The branch of fiqh that is set in contrast to specific issues, similarly al-jins which is placed for a universal that is accepted in answer to 'what is it?' over many different realities, and al-naw' which is placed for a universal that is transferred in answer to 'what is it?' over many agreeing realities. Under conceptual essences, examples of composites from several matters are given, so one should not imagine that conceptual essences are only composites; rather, conceptual essences are also simples. Moreover, the truth is that these simples are called conceptual matters, not conceptual essences. After this introduction: The thing that the positor (wadi') conceives and imagines so that he may place a name in correspondence to it, that imagined thing either is a real essence in terms of the thing itself or not. On the first, when its essence is real, then the conceiver either conceives the very reality of the thing or its accidents and considerations, i.e., accidents, or a composite of the two. In that case, defining the named thing's real essence insofar as it is a real essence is a real definition (ta'rif haqiqi). It benefits the mental depiction and formation of the quiddity, either by all essential properties as in a complete definition, or by some essential properties as in an incomplete definition, or by accidents, or by a composite of accidents and essentials as in descriptive definitions (rusum). And definition of the meaning of the name: if the purpose of definition is only to clarify the meaning of the name and the conceived entity for which the name is placed, then it is a nominal definition (ta'rif ismi). It benefits clarification, i.e., it explains that for which the name is placed with a more well-known term, like 'al-ghadanfar' (lion) or with a term that contains the elaboration of the name's signification, like 'the principle is that on which another is based'. So definitions of non-existents (ma'dumat) are only nominal because they have no established realities, only concepts. And definitions of existents can be both: nominal and real, because they have concepts and realities. If only clarifying the concept is intended, it is nominal; if explaining the reality is desired, it is real. For you might say: the commentator (sharh) said that definitions of existents are sometimes nominal and sometimes real; this is the point of objection. Summary of objection: the author's apparent wording opposes this because in dividing definitions he said: 'either real like the definition of real essences, or nominal like the definition of conceptual entities'. Since definitions of conceptual entities are only nominal, not real, the contrast in the author's wording necessitates that definitions of real essences (i.e., existent and established) are only real, not nominal. I say (response): there is scope to depart from the author's apparent wording by considering a qualification of perspective, meaning: definition of real essences insofar as they are real essences is always real; or it can be said that definitions of essences are mostly real, not universally and invariably; or it can be said that the author's expression is illustrative, not restrictive and perpetual. However, the investigation: if no interpretation and departure from the apparent is made in the author's wording, then it is contrary to investigation. Because the truth is that a real essence is sometimes taken insofar as it is the reality and essence of the named thing established in itself, i.e., no rational consideration intervenes in it; then its definition is only real, not nominal, because it is the answer to 'ma haqiqiyya' which is posited for seeking the reality. And the answer to 'ma haqiqiyya' is always a real definition, not nominal. Rather, nominal definition belongs to 'ma sharhiat ismiyya' which is posited for asking for the explanation of the name and clarification of the concept, which precedes 'ma haqiqiyya' by two degrees; its answer is a nominal definition. And these inquiries: the order among the instruments of inquiry according to the logicians is: since an absolute unknown cannot be sought, a concept of the sought must be present in the mind in some way; hence explanation of the name (sharh ismi) is necessary, otherwise it cannot be sought. For seeking this concept and explanation of the name, 'ma sharhiat ismiyya' is devised, which precedes all mother inquiries. Once the explanation of the name is achieved, inquiry into its reality cannot be conducted until its existence in itself is affirmed, because reality and essence belong to existents; non-existents have no established reality, only concepts. Therefore, before seeking the reality, affirmation of existence is necessary. For seeking this affirmation of existence in itself, among the mother inquiries, 'hal basita' is devised. So 'hal basita' is posterior to 'ma sharhiat ismiyya' and prior to 'ma haqiqiyya'. After affirmation of existence in itself is obtained, now inquiry into the reality can be conducted, for which 'ma haqiqiyya' is devised. Hence, the definition occurring in answer to 'ma haqiqiyya' is always a real definition. And 'ma haqiqiyya' is posterior to 'hal basita' which seeks the existence of the thing, which is posterior to 'ma' that seeks explanation of the name, i.e., the ismi 'ma' which precedes 'hal basita'. And 'qad yurkhadhu min haythu annahu mafhum al-ism' (and it may be taken insofar as it is the meaning of the name).
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition on the two types of definition (ta'rif) in usul al-fiqh: haqiqi (real) and ismi (nominal). The author begins by distinguishing between jins (genus) and naw' (species) as universals, then moves to conceptual essences (mahiyat i'tibariyya)—noting they can be simple or composite, though simples are better called 'amur i'tibariyya'. The core teaching: a definition is haqiqi when it explains the real essence (mahiyat haqiqiyya) of a thing as it is in itself, using essential properties (dhatiyyat) or accidents, forming complete/incomplete definitions or descriptive definitions (rusum). A definition is ismi when it merely clarifies the meaning of the name (mafhum al-ism) using a more well-known term or an elaboration. The text then applies this: non-existents (ma'dumat) can only have ismi definitions since they lack real essences; existents (mawjudat) can have both depending on the intent—if clarifying the concept, ismi; if explaining the reality, haqiqi. The commentator raises an objection: the author's earlier division seemed to restrict real definitions to real essences and nominal to conceptual ones, contradicting the claim that existents can have both. The response offers three harmonizing approaches: (1) qualify 'insofar as they are real essences', (2) say it's the majority not universal, (3) treat it as illustrative not exhaustive. The true investigation (tahqiq) resolves: a real essence taken absolutely (without mental consideration) yields only a haqiqi definition because it answers 'ma haqiqiyya', which demands reality; whereas an ismi definition answers 'ma sharhiat ismiyya', which seeks name clarification. This leads into the logical order of inquiry: first, explanation of the name (sharh ismi) via 'ma sharhiat ismiyya'; second, verification of existence via 'hal basita'; third, inquiry into the essence via 'ma haqiqiyya'. This order is essential for proper definition classification in Hanafi usul, ensuring that definitions are applied correctly based on the nature of the thing and the question asked.

Key Terms
تعریف حقیقی (ta'rif haqiqi): A definition that explains the real essence (mahiyat haqiqiyya) of a thing as it is in itself, answering 'what is it?' with essential properties (dhatiyyat) or accidents.
تعریف اسمی (ta'rif ismi): A definition that merely clarifies the meaning of the name (mafhum al-ism) by a more well-known term or elaboration, without explicating the real essence.
ما حقیقیہ (ma haqiqiyya): An inquiry tool seeking the real essence of a thing, requiring a haqiqi definition in response.
ما اسمیہ (ma ismiyya): An inquiry tool seeking explanation of the name (sharh ismi), the first step in investigating an unknown thing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the passage, what type of definition applies to non-existents (ma'dumat)?
A) Only haqiqi
B) Only ismi
C) Both haqiqi and ismi
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
Definitions in Hanafi usul are of two types: haqiqi for real essences, ismi for names; the logical inquiry into an unknown proceeds from name to existence to essence.

Method of Learning
intermediate
10 min
Haqiqi vs Ismi Definitions and the Order of Inquiry
Explaining the distinction between haqiqi and ismi definitions and the logical order of questioning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between haqiqi and ismi definitions and correctly sequence the three interrogative tools (ma ismiyya sharha, hal basita, ma haqiqiyya) in the logical order of defining an unknown.

Core Idea
A haqiqi definition reveals the essence of an existent; an ismi definition explains a name; one must ask for the meaning, then verify existence, then ask for the essence.

This passage from a commentary on al-Ta'ziyah wa al-Talwih explains a foundational logical concept: the difference between defining the reality of a thing and defining the meaning of its name. It also establishes the necessary order of questioning in Islamic jurisprudence and logic. Understanding this sequence is crucial for correctly applying definitions in legal reasoning (istidlal).

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two definition types
Identify that a haqiqi (real) definition answers the question about the essence of an existent thing, while an ismi (nominal) definition explains the meaning of a name, regardless of existence.
The distinction hinges on whether the definition presupposes existence or not.
2
Identify the three interrogative tools
Learn the three tools: ma ismiyya sharha (asks for meaning of the name), hal basita (asks if the thing exists), and ma haqiqiyya (asks for the real essence).
Each tool has a specific role and order.
3
Sequence the inquiry
Understand that one must first seek the explanation of the name (ma ismiyya), then verify existence (hal basita), then ask about the reality (ma haqiqiyya). This order is necessary because you cannot seek the reality of something without knowing what its name means and confirming that it exists.
This sequence is a key principle in logic and usul al-fiqh.
4
Apply to the triangle example
See how the definition of triangle ('a figure enclosed by three sides') is initially ismi when used in geometry; after geometry proves the existence of triangles, the same definition becomes haqiqi because it now answers the real essence.
The same linguistic formulation can shift from ismi to haqiqi based on context.

تعریف اسمی واقع ہوتی ہے۔ اِن مطالب یعنی آلات طلب میں اہل میزان کے نزدیک ترتیب یہ ہے چونکہ مجہول مطلق کی طلب نہیں ہو سکتی اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ مطلوب کا تصور بوجہ ما ذہن میں ہونا چاہیئے اس لئے مطلوب کی شرح اسم ضروری ہے ورنہ اس کی طلب نہیں ہو سکتی اور اس تصور اور شرح اسم کی طلب کے لئے ما شارحہ اسمیہ کی وضع کی گئی ہے جو تمام امہات المطالب سے مقدم ہے جب شرح اسم ہو جائے گی تو اس کی حقیقت کی طلب اور دریافت نہیں کی جاسکتی جب تک اس کے وجود فی نفسہ کی تصدیق نہ ہو جائے کیونکہ حقیقت اور ماہیت موجودات کی ہوتی ہے معدومات کی کوئی حقیقت ثابتہ نہیں ہوتی بلکہ ان کے صرف مفہومات ہوتے ہیں لہذا طلب حقیقت سے نفسہ کے حاصل ہو جانے کے بعد اب طلب حقیقت ہو سکتی ہے جس کے لئے ما حقیقیہ کی وضع ہے تو ما حقیقیہ کے جواب میں جو تعریف واقع ہوتی ہے وہ ہمیشہ تعریف حقیقی ہوتی ہے۔ وھی ای ما الحقیقیه متاخرة عن هل البسيطة الطالبة لوجود الشئ المتأخرة یہ صفت ہے محل بسیطہ کی عن ما التي لطلب تفسير الاسم یہ وہی ما اسمیہ ہے جو حل بسیطہ سے مقدم ہے۔ وقدیر خذ من حيث انها مفهوم الاسم اور کبھی ماہیت حقیقیہ بایں حیثیت اخذ کی جاتی شارح وهذا التعريف قد يكون الا يعني بيبي تعریف اسمی کبھی حقیقت شی کا عین ہوتی ہے یہ اس وقت ہوتا ہے جب کہ متعقل واضع عین حقیقت ہو وقد يكون غيرها یعنی کبھی تعریف اسمی غیر حقیقت ہوتی ہے۔ ولهذا صرحوا بانه قد تحرام اس لئے اہل فن نے تصریح کی ہے کہ کبھی تعریف حقیقی اور اسمی آپس میں متحد ہو جاتی ہیں ۔ الا انه مگر اتنی فرق ضرور ہے کہ وجود شی کے علم اور تصدیق سے قبل اسمی کہلاتی ہے اور وہی تعریف بعد العلم
