کے وجود پر دلیل پیش کر دیتا ہے تو یہی تعریف اسمی اس وقت حقیقی ہو جاتی ہے۔
Its definition is only ismi, not haqiqi. So the comparison present in the author's expression demands that the definition of real quiddities, i.e., existent and established things, is only haqiqi, not ismi. I said: the summary of the answer is that there is room for deviation from the author's apparent expression by considering a restriction of aspect. The meaning would be: the definition of real quiddities, in their aspect as real quiddities, is always haqiqi. Or it could be said that the definition of quiddities is usually haqiqi, not universally and necessarily. Or it could be said that the author's expression is intended as an example, not as exclusive and perpetual. But upon investigation, if the author's expression is not interpreted and deviated from the apparent, then it is contrary to investigation. Because the investigation is that a real quiddity is sometimes taken in the aspect that it is the reality of the named thing and the established quiddity in itself, meaning that the intellect's consideration has no role in it. Then at that time, its definition is only haqiqi, not ismi, because it is the answer to 'ma' which seeks reality. Since it is the answer to 'ma haqiqiyya', which is placed for seeking reality, and in the answer to 'ma haqiqiyya', a haqiqi definition always occurs; it cannot be ismi. Rather, the ismi definition is for 'ma sharhah ismiyya', which is placed for explaining the name and expressing the concept, and which is two steps prior to 'ma haqiqiyya'; in its answer, an ismi definition occurs. These demands: among the instruments of seeking, according to the logicians, the order is as follows: since absolute unknown cannot be sought, it is necessary that there be a mental concept of the sought by some means. Therefore, an explanation of the name of the sought is necessary; otherwise, it cannot be sought. For seeking this mental concept and explanation of the name, 'ma sharhah ismiyya' is placed, which is prior to all mother-principles. When the explanation of the name is done, its reality cannot be sought until its existence in itself is verified. Because reality and quiddity belong to existents; non-existents have no established reality, but only concepts. Hence, before seeking reality, verification of existence is necessary. For this verification of existence in itself, among the mother-principles, 'hal basita' is placed. So 'hal basita' is later than 'ma sharhah ismiyya' and earlier than 'ma haqiqiyya'. After obtaining verification of existence in itself, now reality can be sought, for which 'ma haqiqiyya' is placed. Thus, the definition that occurs in answer to 'ma haqiqiyya' is always haqiqi. And that 'ma haqiqiyya' is later than 'hal basita' which seeks existence, and 'hal basita' is later than 'ma' that seeks explanation of the name, which is the same 'ma ismiyya' that is prior to 'hal basita'. And it is taken in the aspect that it is the concept of the name. And sometimes a real quiddity is taken in the aspect that it is the concept of the name, and at the time of placing the name, this is the object of the placer's intention. Then in this regard, its definition is certainly ismi; it is the answer to that 'ma' which is placed for seeking the concept of the name and the object of the placer, i.e., 'ma ismiyya sharha'. And this definition may be 'ala yani'? an ismi definition sometimes is the very reality of the thing; this occurs when the object of the placer is the very reality, and sometimes it is other than reality, i.e., sometimes an ismi definition is other than reality. For this reason, they have stated that sometimes haqiqi and ismi definitions unite with each other. However, there is a necessary difference: before the knowledge and verification of the thing's existence, it is called ismi, and that same definition after knowledge of the thing's existence becomes haqiqi. For example, the definition of triangle: 'a figure enclosed by three sides, i.e., three lines' in geometry is called an ismi definition. After demonstration of its existence, i.e., when the science of geometry presents a proof of the existence of this triangle, then this same ismi definition becomes haqiqi.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage discusses the distinction between real (haqiqi) and nominal (ismi) definitions, and the logical order of interrogative tools used to define an unknown. The author begins by addressing a potential contradiction: if the definition of quiddities is only ismi, then the comparison with the author's text would require that real quiddities (existing things) have only haqiqi definitions. To resolve this, the commentator offers several interpretations: the restriction to ismi definitions may be understood as a mere example, not universal; or it may be that definitions of quiddities are usually haqiqi, but not always; or the author's expression can be interpreted by considering the aspect (bi-haysiyya) of the quiddity. The commentator then presents the investigation: a real quiddity can be taken in two ways—either as the reality itself (in which case its definition is haqiqi, answering 'ma haqiqiyya') or as the concept of the name (in which case its definition is ismi, answering 'ma ismiyya sharha'). The passage then explains the three-tiered order of questioning according to logicians: first, 'ma sharhah ismiyya' to get a nominal explanation; second, 'hal basita' to verify existence; third, 'ma haqiqiyya' to seek the real essence. This hierarchy is necessary because one cannot seek the reality of something without first knowing what the name means and confirming that the thing exists. The commentator also notes that sometimes a nominal definition coincides with a real definition when the name's concept exactly matches the reality, but the distinction remains based on prior or posterior knowledge of existence.

Key Terms
تعریف حقیقی (ta'rif haqiqi): A definition that answers 'ma haqiqiyya' and describes the real essence of an existent thing.
تعریف اسمی (ta'rif ismi): A definition that answers 'ma ismiyya sharha' and explains the meaning of a name, regardless of whether the thing exists.
ما حقیقیہ (ma haqiqiyya): An interrogative particle used to ask about the reality/essence of a thing, presupposing its existence.
ما اسمیہ شارحہ (ma ismiyya sharha): An interrogative particle used to ask for the explanation of the meaning of a name, placed prior to verification of existence.
ہل بسیطہ (hal basita): An interrogative particle used to ask whether a thing exists (verification of existence), placed between 'ma sharhah' and 'ma haqiqiyya'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which interrogative tool must be used first when seeking to define an unknown?
A) ما حقیقیہ
B) ما اسمیہ شارحہ
C) ہل بسیطہ
D) ما شارحہ

Key Takeaway
The logical order of inquiry is: first explain the name (ma ismiyya), then verify existence (hal basita), then ask about the essence (ma haqiqiyya); the definition type depends on which stage you are at.

The Qualifiers of the Definition of Fiqh
Explaining the qualifiers in the definition of fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each qualifier in the Hanafi definition of fiqh, explain its purpose (maqsad), and apply it to distinguish fiqh from other types of knowledge.

Core Idea
Fiqh is only practical shar‘i rulings derived from detailed evidences — not beliefs, not taqlid.

Fiqh is defined with precision to separate it from other sciences and from blind following. This lesson unpacks each qualifier in the classical definition, showing how each word excludes a specific type of knowledge. Understanding these boundaries is essential for proper legal reasoning and avoids conflating fiqh with theology, logic, or mere imitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and its qualifiers
The core definition is: al-ilm bil-ahkam al-shar'iyyah al-amaliyyah min adillatiha al-tafşiliyyah. List each qualifier: 'ahkam', 'shar'iyyah', 'amaliyyah', 'min adillatiha al-tafşiliyyah'. Understand the structure of the definition.
These qualifiers are known as qayud al-ih tirayziyyah (precautionary qualifiers) each excluding a specific category.
2
Explain the purpose of 'ahkam'
The qualifier 'ahkam' (rulings) excludes knowledge that pertains to non-rulings, such as conceptual knowledge of essences and attributes (e.g., knowledge of Allah's attributes). Fiqh concerns rulings, not mere concepts.
This excludes 'ilm tasawwuri' (conceptual knowledge).
3
Explain the purpose of 'shar'iyyah'
The qualifier 'shar'iyyah' (shar‘i) excludes non-shar‘i rulings, i.e., those that are not derived from the Shari‘ah but are prerequisites for it, such as the obligation of faith (wujub al-iman). Such rulings are not dependent on the Shari‘ah; rather the Shari‘ah depends on them.
This ensures fiqh deals only with rulings that originate from the Shari‘ah (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas).
4
Explain the purpose of 'amaliyyah'
The qualifier 'amaliyyah' (practical) excludes theoretical (nazari) shar‘i rulings, such as the knowledge that consensus (ijma) is a proof. These are principles of usul al-fiqh or beliefs, not practical rulings.
This distinguishes fiqh from usul al-fiqh and theology.
5
Explain the purpose of 'min adillatiha al-tafşiliyyah'
This qualifier ensures that the knowledge of rulings must be derived from detailed, specific evidences (the four sources: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) in a manner that involves ijtihad. It excludes taqlid (following a mujtahid without knowing the evidence) and knowledge from summary evidences (adillah ijmaliah) that do not specify the ruling.
The added qualifier 'bil-istidlāl' (by inference) by Ibn al-Hajib is considered redundant because knowledge from evidence is inherently inferential.

اصلیہ کہا جاتا ہے جیسے كون الاجماع حجة والایمان واجبا اسی طرح فقہ اصطلاحی کی تعریف سے اللہ تعالیٰ کا علم اور جبریل کا اور رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا اور اسی طرح علم مقلد بھی خارج ہو جائے گا کیونکہ یہ ادلہ تفصیلیہ سے حاصل نہیں ہیں کیونکہ ادلہ سے حاصل ہونے والا علم استدلالی ہوتا ہے اور علم اللہ و علم جبریل و علم الرسول یہ استدلالی نہیں ہیں بلکہ یہ علوم ضروریہ اور بدیہیہ ہیں فقہ تو علم استدلالی و اکتسابی کا نام ہے نہ کہ ضروریات اور بدیہیات کا اور مقلد کا علم قول مجتہد سے حاصل ہے نہ کہ ادلہ اربعہ سے۔ قوله يمكن ان يراد بالحكم الو حکم کا اطلاق مختلف معانی پر ہوتا ہے عرف ناس میں اس کا اطلاق اسناد امرالی آخر پر ہوتا ہے یعنی ایک امر کی دوسرے کی طرف نسبتہ کرنا خواہ یہ نسبته بالایجاب ہو یا بالسلب یہ عرفی معنیٰ کہلاتا ہے دوسرا اصطلاحی یعنی اہل اصول کی اصطلاح میں حکم کا اطلاق خطا الله تعالى المتعلق بافعال المكلفين بالاقتضاء او التغییر پر ہوتا ہے اور تیسرا منطقی یعنی اہل منطق کی اصطلاح میں حکم کا اطلاق ادراک ان النسبة واقعہ اولیست بواقعہ پر ہوتا ہے اور اسی کا نام وہ تصدیق رکھتے ہیں۔ وهو ليس بمواد[؟] ههنا یعنی حکم منطقی تو یہاں مراد نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ حکم منطقی از قبیلہ علم والادراک ہے تو اس صورت میں فقہ کی تعریف کا حاصل ہو گا علم بالعلوم الشرعیة حالانکہ یہ صحیح نہیں ہے
The purpose is to explain the benefit of the qualifier 'shar'iyyah' along with this interpretation. So it is said that the ruling according to this interpretation of the address of Allah Almighty is of two types: one is shar'i, whose interpretation is 'the address of Allah Almighty regarding what depends on the Shari'ah', i.e., addressing things whose establishment is dependent on the Shari'ah, like the obligation of prayer and zakat etc. The second is non-shar'i, its interpretation is 'the address of Allah Almighty regarding what does not depend on the Shari'ah', like the obligation of faith and the obligation of concepts [concerning?] the Prophet (peace be upon him). These are things that are not dependent on the Shari'ah, but rather the Shari'ah depends on them, because until faith in Allah and belief in the Prophet are established, the Shari'ah cannot be established. For the Shari'ah is the command of God and the command of the Messenger, and the person who does not accept God and the Messenger cannot accept the Shari'ah. So the qualifier 'shar'iyyah' will exclude from the definition of fiqh the knowledge of those non-shar'i rulings, i.e., those that are not dependent on the Shari'ah but rather the Shari'ah depends on them, from the scope of fiqh. Then the shar'i is either nazari – the benefit of the qualifier 'amaliyyah' is being explained. The summary is that the shar'i ruling in the mentioned sense is of two types: one is nazari, which intends a theory and belief, like the knowledge that consensus is a proof – this is nazari. The second type is 'amali, i.e., that which intends action upon it. The qualifier 'amaliyyah' will exclude those nazari shar'i rulings from fiqh. His statement 'min adillatiha' – this is the benefit of the qualifier 'min adillatiha', and the prepositional phrase 'min adillatiha' is attached to 'al-'ilm'. The meaning will be that the knowledge of a person described by this knowledge is obtained from those specific evidences, i.e., the four sources, so with this qualifier, taqlidi knowledge will be excluded from fiqh. Because the muqallid, although the statement of the mujtahid is a proof for him, but this proof, i.e., the statement of the mujtahid, is not from among the four evidences. His statement 'al-tafṣīliyyah' – this qualifier excludes that knowledge of rulings which is obtained from summary evidences (adillah ijmaliah), like the knowledge obtained from the muqtada or nafi, because these are not detailed evidences. And Ibn al-Hajib added – Ibn al-Hajib gave this same definition of fiqh, but after 'min adillatiha al-tafṣīliyyah' he added the qualifier 'bil-istidlāl'. Regarding this the author said: 'No doubt it is redundant' because the knowledge that is obtained from the evidence is always inferential (istidlali), so adding 'bil-istidlāl' after 'min adillatiha al-tafṣīliyyah' is a useless repetition. The commentator said in al-Talwih: 'His statement before: al-'ilm...' The definition of fiqh is transmitted from the Shafi'i scholars. And the explanation of that is that the benefit of the precautionary qualifiers becomes clear: the object of knowledge is either a ruling or a non-ruling. So the qualifier 'ahkam' will exclude knowledge that pertains to non-rulings, i.e., conceptual sciences. Then the ruling is either shar'i, i.e., taken from the Shari'ah, or else it is non-shar'i. Then the shar'i's relation is either to the quality of action or not; the first is called 'amali, the second is non-'amali. Then knowledge of the 'amali ruling is either known from its detailed evidence on which its knowledge depends, or not. Now the summary of the definition is that fiqh is a knowledge that pertains to all practical shar'i rulings, and this knowledge is obtained from detailed evidences. Now that knowledge which pertains not to rulings but to essences and attributes, i.e., conceptual knowledge of them, will be excluded from the definition of fiqh. Similarly, knowledge that pertains to rulings but not to shar'i rulings, rather to rational rulings like the knowledge that the world is originated, or pertains to sensory rulings like the knowledge that fire burns, or that knowledge which pertains to rulings taken from convention and terminology, which are called terminological or positive rulings like the knowledge that the subject is in the nominative – all these will be outside fiqh because they do not pertain to shar'i rulings. Similarly, knowledge that pertains to shar'i rulings but they are not practical, rather they are theoretical, which are called doctrinal and fundamental, like knowledge that consensus is a proof and that faith is obligatory, will also be outside fiqh. Similarly, from the terminological definition of fiqh, the knowledge of Allah, Gabriel, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and likewise the knowledge of the muqallid will be excluded, because they are not obtained from detailed evidences. Since the knowledge obtained from evidences is inferential, and the knowledge of Allah, Gabriel, and the Messenger is not inferential; rather they are necessary and intuitive sciences. Fiqh is the name of inferential and acquired knowledge, not of necessities and intuitions. And the muqallid's knowledge is obtained from the statement of the mujtahid, not from the four evidences. His statement: 'It is possible that by 'hukm' is meant...' The term 'hukm' applies to different meanings. In common parlance ('urf al-nās), it applies to the attribution of one thing to another, whether positively or negatively – this is called the 'urfi meaning. Second is the terminological meaning (iṣṭilāḥī): in the terminology of the scholars of uṣūl, 'hukm' applies to the address of Allah Almighty related to the actions of the legally responsible persons by way of demand or option. Third is the logical meaning (manṭiqī): in the terminology of logicians, 'hukm' applies to the perception of the relation being actual or not actual, and they call this 'taṣdīq'. And it is not intended here – meaning the logical 'hukm' cannot be intended here, because the logical 'hukm' is of the category of knowledge and perception. In that case, the definition of fiqh would become 'knowledge of shar'i sciences', which is not correct.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary (sharh) on the definition of fiqh, explaining each qualifier (qayd) and its purpose. The author begins by clarifying the qualifier 'shar'iyyah', which restricts rulings to those derived from the Shari'ah, thereby excluding foundational beliefs like the obligation of faith (wujub al-iman) that are prerequisites for the Shari'ah itself. Next, the qualifier 'amaliyyah' excludes theoretical (nazari) rulings such as the evidentiary value of consensus (kawn al-ijma' hujjah), confining fiqh to practical matters. Then 'min adillatiha al-tafṣīliyyah' ensures that knowledge is derived from specific, detailed evidences (the four sources), excluding taqlid (blind following) and knowledge from summary evidences. The comment on Ibn al-Hajib's addition of 'bil-istidlāl' is explained as redundant because any knowledge from evidence is inherently inferential. Finally, the passage discusses the multiple meanings of 'hukm' (customary, usuli, and logical) and clarifies that only the usuli meaning applies here, avoiding the circular definition 'knowledge of shar'i sciences' that would result from the logical meaning.

Key Terms
حكم شرعي (ḥukm sharʿī): The address of Allah related to the actions of the legally responsible persons by way of demand or option (قتضاء أو تخيير).
أدلة تفصيلية (adillah tafṣīliyyah): The specific, detailed evidences from which a ruling is derived, primarily the four sources: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas.
تقليد (taqlīd): Following a mujtahid without knowing the detailed evidence; such knowledge is not considered fiqh in the technical sense.
نظري (nazarī): Theoretical; a ruling that concerns belief or principle, not action, e.g., that Ijma is a proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the qualifier 'amaliyyah' (practical) exclude from the definition of fiqh?
A) Knowledge derived from taqlid
B) Theoretical (nazari) shar'i rulings like the evidentiary value of consensus
C) Non-shar'i rulings like the obligation of faith
D) Knowledge from summary evidences

Key Takeaway
Fiqh is defined precisely by qualifiers: it must be knowledge of practical (amali) shar‘i rulings derived from detailed evidences (adillah tafṣīliyyah), excluding beliefs, theoretical principles, and mere imitation.

Defense of the Definition of Fiqh: Addressing Four Objections
Commentary defending the definition of fiqh against four objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the four objections to the definition of fiqh, state the Hanafi responses, and apply the distinction between real and codified fiqh to evaluate the scope of the definition.

Core Idea
A valid definition of fiqh allows for growth, excludes analogical rulings as 'real' fiqh, and conditions ijma only when it occurs.

In this passage, the commentator defends the author's definition of fiqh as 'knowledge of the rulings of revelation and, if it exists, ijma' against four logical objections. Each objection attacks a different aspect—static nature, applicability to the Companions, exclusion of qiyas, and ambiguity of 'appearance'. The responses clarify key distinctions: ta'yin naw'i vs shakhsi, conditionality of ijma, real vs codified fiqh, and direct appearance to the mujtahid.

Guided Path
1
Identify each objection and its basis
Read each of the four objections in the passage. Note what aspect of the definition is being challenged and the reasoning behind the objection.
The objections are: (1) static nature, (2) ijma condition, (3) exclusion of qiyas, (4) ambiguity of 'appearance'.
2
State the commentator's response for each
For each objection, extract the commentator's rebuttal. Pay attention to key distinctions like ta'yin naw'i, conditional ijma, and real vs codified fiqh.
3
Recognize the key distinctions used
Identify the critical conceptual pairs: ta'yin shakhsi vs ta'yin naw'i, fiqh haqiqi vs mudawwan, and the conditionality of ijma.
These distinctions resolve the apparent contradictions in the definition.
4
Apply the distinction between real and codified fiqh
Given a new ruling derived by qiyas, determine whether it belongs to real fiqh or codified fiqh based on the commentator's criteria.
Real fiqh: directly from revelation/certain ijma. Codified fiqh: includes qiyas and other inferred rulings.
5
Evaluate the overall coherence of the definition
Assess whether the definition, after the responses, consistently covers all necessary aspects of fiqh and remains epistemologically sound.
Consider whether the definition could be improved or if it successfully balances comprehensiveness and precision.

وہ علم مخصوص اور معین ہے ۔ جواب از اعتراض اول :- شارح نے جو یہ کہا ہے کہ اسم لعلم مخصوص اس سے کیا مراد اگر مراد شارح تعیین شخصی ہے جو عدد معين من الاحکام میں محصور ہو جو قابل زیادہ نہ ہوں تو یہ مراد صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ تمام علوم مدونہ علم کلی ہیں جو تلاحق افکار کے ساتھ حينا فحيناً قابل زيادة ہوتے ہیں یہی وجہ ہے کہ اسماء علوم کو اعلام جنسیہ کہا جاتا ہے علم شخصی نہیں کہا جاتا اگر تعیین سے مراد تعیین نوعی ہے یعنی ایک موضوع کے اعراض ذاتیہ سے بحث کی جاتی ہے جس کی بنا پر وہ دوسرے علوم سے ممتاز ہو جاتا ہے تو اس قسم کی تعیین تبدل بحسب الاعصار والایام کے منافی نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کے اندر زیادۃ و نقص ہو سکتا ہے آخر وہ صحابہ جو بالاتفاق فقیہ ہیں۔ ان کے علوم بحسب نزول الاحكام يوماً فيوماً زیادہ ہوتے رہتے تھے اور جب کوئی مسئلہ مفتوح ہو جاتا تو کمی واقع ہو جاتی تھی بہر حال زيادة و نقص تعیین نوعی کے منافی نہیں ہے علاوہ ازیں نسخ کی صورت میں علم بالناسخ والمنسوخ مجتہد فقیہ کے لئے ضروری ہے تو اس صورت میں نقص في العلم واقع نہیں ہوگا اور زیادۃ فی العلوم تو ہوتی رہتی ہے جس کا انکار نہیں کیا جا سکتا۔ الثاني إن التعريف الا یہ دوسرا اعتراض ہے حاصل اس کا یہ ہے کہ یہ تعریف فقہ صحابہ پر صادق نہیں آتی کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی زندگی میں اجماع کا وجود ہی نہیں تھا حالانکہ مصنف نے علم بالاحكام التي انعقد علیہ الاجماع کو ضروری قرار دیا ہے لہزار سول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے زمانہ میں جو صحابہ فقیہ تھے ان کی فقہ پر یہ تعریف صادق نہیں آئے گی ۔ کانہ اراد گویا کہ مصنف کی مراد یہ ہوگی کہ فقہ صرف علم بما ظہر بہ نزول الوحی کا نام ہے اگر اجماع نہ ہو اور اگر جماع ہو تو پھر علم بما ظہر بہ نزول الوحی اور بما انعقد علیہ الاجماع کا نام فقہ ہو گا اور اس قسم کی تشکیکات تعریفات میں بعید ہیں۔ اس کا جواب دیا گیا ہے کہ مصنف کی مراد یہی مفہوم ہے کما صرح به في التوست ولا بعد في التعريف بمثل ہذا کیونکہ یہ امر مشہور ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے زمانہ میں صحابہ کے اندر فقہ اور اجتہاد موجود تھا حالانکہ اس وقت اجماع کا وجود نہیں تھا تو اس سے واضح ہو جاتا ہے مراد یہی ہے کہ علم بما انعقد علیہ الاجتماع اس وقت ضروری ہے جب اجتماع موجود ہو اگر موجود نہ ہو تو اس کا علم شرط نہیں ہے اس شہرت کی وجہ سے اس مراد میں کوئی بعد نہیں ہے علاوہ ازیں مصنف کا قول والتي انعقد علیہ الاجماع سے مراد ہے والتي انعقد علیہ الاجماع عند تحققہ تو اب مفہوم تعریف یہ ہوگا کہ فقہ علم ہے بماظہر یہ نزول الوحی کا در آنحالیکہ وہ مقرون ہو علم بالاحکام التي انعقد علیہ الاجماع کے ساتھ علی تقدیر تحقق الاجماع تو اس وقت یہ تعریف فقہ صحابہ پر صادق آجائے گی۔ الثالث یہ تیسرا اعتراض ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ اس تعریف مصنف کے لحاظ سے علم بالاحکام القیاسیہ خارج از فقہ ہو جائے گا حالانکہ عبد العلماء یہی فقہ کے معظم مسائل ہیں۔ الا ان يقال سے شارح نے اس اعتراض کے جواب دینے کی کوشش کی ہے خلاصہ اس کا یہ ہے کہ یہ مسائل اس مجتہد کے نزدیک فقہ ہیں جس کا اجتہاد ان مسائل تک پہنچا ہے یہ علی الاطلاق فقہ نہیں ہیں تو اس وقت یہ لازم آئے گا کہ ہر مجتہد کی فقہ الگ الگ ہو جائے گی جواب اس کا یہ ہے کہ مسائل قیاسیہ چونکہ مجتہد کی فقا اور اجتہاد کا نتیجہ ہیں لہذا یہ مسائل داخل فی الفقہ الحقیقی نہیں ہو سکتے بلکہ ان کا خروج عن الفقہ ضروری ہے ورنہ تو دور لازم آئے گا کہامر۔ البتہ جب علم فقہ مدون و مبوب ہوا تو اس فقہ مدونہ میں اسے درج کر دیا گیا چونکہ عوام الناس اپنے اعمال تکلیفیہ میں ان کی طرف ایسے محتاج تھے جیسے مسائل فقہیہ حقیقیہ کی طرف محتاج تھے ۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ فقہ حقیقی سے خارج ہیں اور فقہ مدد نہ میں داخل ہیں اور فقہ مدونہ ہر مجتہد کی الگ الگ ہونے میں کوئی قباحت نہیں ہے جیسے فقہ حنفی فقہ شافعی اور مالکی سے الگ ہے اور اسی طرح ائمہ اربعہ کی فقہ الگ الگ ہے اس میں کوئی قباحت متصور نہیں ہوتی ۔ الرابع انه ان اریدا یہ چوتھا اعتراض ہے اور اس کا منشا ظهر به نزول الوحی کا لفظ یہ ہے کہ ظہور سے کیا مراد ہے اگر اس سے مراد ظہور فی الجملہ ہے یعنی علی البعض تو پھر بہت سے فقہاء صحابہ ان احکام کو نہیں جانتے تھے جن کے ساتھ نزول الوحی فی الجملہ یعنی علی بعض الصحابہ ظاہر ہو چکی تھی جیسے کہ صحابہ نے بہت سے مسائل میں ام المؤمنین عائشہ صدیقہ رضی اللہ عنہا کی طرف رجوع کیا اور انہوں نے ان مسائل کو حل فرما دیا تو کیا ان صحابہ کو فقیہ نہیں کہا جائے گا جو ان مسائل کو نہ جانتے تھے حالانکہ وہ بالاتفاق فقیہ تھے اور اگر ظہور وحی سے مراد ظہور علی الاعم والاغلب ہے یعنی اکثرا فراد صحابہ پر اس کا ظہور مراد ہے۔ فهو غير مضبوط یعنی اکثر کی کوئی تعداد شحت الضبط نہیں آسکتی کیونکہ رواۃ کثیر التعداد ہیں جو اپنے اسفار و اشتغال میں متفرق رہتے تھے پھر اگر یہ تسلیم کر بھی لیا جائے تو وہ حکم جو مروی علی طریقہ الاحاد ہے وہ فقہ میں شمار نہ ہو جب تک کہ شائع ذائع ہو کر ظاہر علی الاکثر نہ ہو ۔ شارت کا یہ اعتراض رابع تو بالکل فضول ہے کیونکہ ظہور وحی سے مراد ظہور المجتہد نفسہ ہے لیکن لا بتوسط القیاس اور ظہور وحی سے مراد نہ ظہور فی الجملہ ہے نہ ظہور علی الاعم الاغلب ہے بلکہ مراد یہ ہے کہ جو مجتہد اور فقیہ ہے اس پر اس کا ظہور ہو جائے ۔ مراد تو یہ واضح تھی معلوم
It is a specific and determined science. Answer to the first objection: The commentator said that 'name of a specific science' — what is meant? If the commentator means personal specificity (ta'yin shakhsi) confined to a fixed number of rulings that cannot be increased, then this meaning is incorrect because all codified sciences are universal sciences that are subject to increase from time to time with the succession of thoughts. This is why the names of sciences are called generic proper nouns (a'lam jinsiyyah), not personal proper nouns. If specificity means specific type (ta'yin naw'i), i.e., discussion of the essential accidents (a'rad dhatiyyah) of a subject by which it is distinguished from other sciences, then this type of specificity is not contrary to change over time and eras; rather, increase and decrease can occur within it. After all, the Companions, who are unanimously jurists, their knowledge used to increase day by day according to the revelation of rulings, and when an issue was resolved, a decrease would occur. In any case, increase and decrease are not contrary to specific type. Moreover, in the case of abrogation, knowledge of the abrogating and abrogated is necessary for a mujtahid jurist, so in that case there will be no decrease in knowledge, and increase in sciences is ongoing, which cannot be denied. Second: This is the second objection. Its summary is that this definition does not apply to the fiqh of the Companions because during the lifetime of the Messenger of God ﷺ there was no ijma, whereas the author made knowledge of rulings upon which there is ijma necessary. Therefore, during the time of the Messenger of God ﷺ, the definition would not apply to those Companions who were jurists. It is as if the author intended that fiqh is only knowledge of what was revealed by revelation if there is no ijma, and if there is ijma, then the name fiqh applies to knowledge of what was revealed by revelation and what was agreed upon by ijma. And such objections to definitions are far-fetched. The answer given is that the author intended this meaning, as he stated clearly in al-Tawdih, and there is no far-fetchedness in a definition like this because it is well-known that during the time of the Messenger of God ﷺ, fiqh and ijtihad existed among the Companions even though ijma did not exist then. So it becomes clear that the intended meaning is that knowledge of what is agreed upon by ijma is necessary when ijma exists; if it does not exist, knowledge of it is not a condition. Due to this well-known fact, there is no far-fetchedness in this meaning. Moreover, the author's statement 'which are agreed upon by ijma' means 'which are agreed upon by ijma when it exists.' So now the meaning of the definition becomes: Fiqh is knowledge of what appears by revelation, while it is accompanied by knowledge of rulings agreed upon by ijma, on the condition that ijma has occurred. Then the definition will apply to the fiqh of the Companions. Third: This is the third objection. Its summary is that according to this definition of the author, knowledge of analogical rulings (ahkam qiyasiyyah) will be excluded from fiqh, whereas according to the scholars, these constitute the majority of fiqh issues. The commentator tried to answer this objection with 'illa an yuqal' — the summary is that these issues are fiqh according to the mujtahid whose ijtihad has reached them; they are not fiqh absolutely. Then it would follow that each mujtahid's fiqh would be different. The answer is that since qiyasi issues are the result of the mujtahid's understanding and ijtihad, they cannot be included in true fiqh (al-fiqh al-haqiqi); rather, their exclusion from fiqh is necessary, otherwise circular reasoning would occur. However, when the science of fiqh was codified and organized into chapters, it was included in this codified fiqh because the common people were as needy of them in their obligatory actions as they were of real fiqh issues. The summary is that they are outside real fiqh and included in codified fiqh, and there is no harm in each mujtahid having a different codified fiqh, just as Hanafi fiqh is different from Shafi‘i and Maliki, and similarly the fiqh of the four imams is different. There is no harm in that. Fourth: This is the fourth objection, and its source is the phrase 'what appears by revelation' (zahara bihi nuzul al-wahi). What is meant by 'appearance'? If it means partial appearance (zuhur fi al-jumlah), i.e., to some people, then many jurist Companions did not know those rulings for which revelation had appeared partially, i.e., to some Companions. For example, the Companions referred to Umm al-Mu'minin ‘A’ishah (may God be pleased with her) in many issues and she resolved them. Would those Companions who did not know these rulings not be called jurists, even though they were unanimously jurists? And if 'appearance of revelation' means appearance to the general majority (zuhur ‘ala al-a‘amm wa al-aghlab), i.e., to most individuals of the Companions, then it is not fixed because the majority cannot be precisely determined, since the narrators are numerous and were scattered in their travels and occupations. Moreover, even if this is accepted, a ruling that is reported as a solitary report (khabar al-wahid) would not be counted as fiqh until it becomes widespread and appears to the majority. The commentator's fourth objection is completely pointless because by 'appearance of revelation' is meant the appearance to the mujtahid himself, but not by way of analogy (qiyas), and 'appearance of revelation' does not mean partial appearance nor appearance to the general majority; rather, it means that it appears to the one who is a mujtahid and jurist. The intended meaning was clear and known.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a commentary defending the definition of fiqh given by the author (likely Sadr al-Shari‘ah in al-Tawdih) against four objections. The commentator addresses each objection in turn:

First objection: The definition says fiqh is a 'specific science' (علم مخصوص). If this means it is fixed and cannot grow, that is false because sciences evolve. The response is that 'specific' means type-specific (تعيين نوعي), not individual-specific, allowing for increase and decrease as seen with the Companions whose knowledge grew with revelation and shrank when issues were settled. Also abrogation doesn't reduce knowledge but adds awareness of abrogation.

Second objection: The definition requires knowledge of ijma, but ijma didn't exist at the time of the Prophet ﷺ, so it wouldn't apply to Companions. The response is that the author's condition of ijma applies only when ijma exists; otherwise, it is not required. This is clarified by the author's statement in al-Tawdih, and it is well-known that the Companions had fiqh and ijtihad without ijma.

Third objection: The definition excludes qiyasi rulings, which form the bulk of fiqh. The response distinguishes between real fiqh (al-fiqh al-haqiqi) — which is direct from revelation — and codified fiqh (al-fiqh al-mudawwan). Qiyasi rulings are the result of ijtihad, so they are not real fiqh themselves but are included in the codified fiqh because people need them. Different schools have different codified fiqh; that's acceptable.

Fourth objection: Ambiguity in 'appearance of revelation' (ظهور الوحي). The objector asks whether it means partial appearance or general majority appearance. The commentator dismisses this as pointless: it means appearance to the individual mujtahid directly, not through analogy. That is clear.

This is typical Hanafi usul discussion defending a definition with logical reasoning and examples from the Companions.

Key Terms
تعيين شخصي (ta'yin shakhsi): Personal specificity: a fixed, unchangeable set of rulings.
تعيين نوعي (ta'yin naw'i): Type specificity: the subject matter and essential accidents that distinguish a science, allowing for growth.
الفقه الحقيقي (al-fiqh al-haqiqi): Real fiqh: knowledge of rulings directly from revelation, not via analogy or ijtihad.
الفقه المدون (al-fiqh al-mudawwan): Codified fiqh: the organized body of law that includes both real and analogical rulings.
ظهور الوحي (zuhur al-wahi): The appearance of revelation to the individual mujtahid directly, not necessarily to others or to the majority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why are qiyasi rulings excluded from 'real fiqh' (al-fiqh al-haqiqi)?
A) Because they are based on ijma, not revelation.
B) Because they are the result of ijtihad and analogy, not direct revelation.
C) Because they are only known to the common people.
D) Because they are not needed for practice.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh, in its real sense, is knowledge directly from revelation and, when present, ijma, while analogical rulings belong to codified fiqh.

The Four Sources of Usul al-Fiqh
Definition of usul al-fiqh sources

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the four primary sources of usul al-fiqh according to the Hanafi school, and state why Qiyas is considered subsidiary.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh: the Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas — with Qiyas as a subsidiary.

This lesson introduces the foundational sources of usul al-fiqh as defined by the Hanafi school. Understanding these sources is essential for grasping how legal rulings are derived. The passage emphasizes that while there are four sources, Qiyas (analogy) depends on the first three.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Recognize that 'usul al-fiqh' refers to the sources and methodology of fiqh, not the rulings themselves.
2
List the four sources
From the passage, extract the four sources: the Book (Quran), Sunnah, Ijma' (consensus), and Qiyas (analogy).
Memorize these as the core sources in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the subsidiary nature of Qiyas
Notice the statement that Qiyas is 'a subsidiary of the three' – it derives rulings from the Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma' and does not stand alone.
This distinguishes Qiyas from primary sources.
4
Connect to the discipline
Relate this definition to the broader field of usul al-fiqh: these sources form the framework for ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال المصنف في التوضيح واصول الفقه الكتاب والسنة والاجماع والقياس وان كان ذا اى القياس فرعا للثلثة اى للكتاب والسنة والإجماع لما ذكر ان اصول الفقه یعنی چونکہ پہلے ذکر ہو چکا ہے کہ اصول فقہ وہ اشیاء ہیں جن پر فقہ کا ابتنار ہے ارادان
The author said in Al-Tawdih: 'And the sources of fiqh are the Book, the Sunnah, consensus, and analogy, although analogy is a subsidiary of the three, i.e., the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus, because it has been mentioned previously that the sources of fiqh are the things upon which fiqh is based.'
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is a definition introducing the four sources of usul al-fiqh according to the Hanafi school. The author quotes from Al-Tawdih, stating that the primary sources are the Quran (al-kitab), the Sunnah, and Ijma' (consensus). Qiyas (analogy) is the fourth source, but it is subsidiary to the first three because it derives rulings from them. The phrase 'as has been mentioned previously' refers to the earlier definition that usul al-fiqh are the foundations upon which fiqh is built. This is a standard Hanafi position that recognizes only these four sources, unlike some other schools that may include additional sources like istihsan or 'urf.

Key Terms
أصول الفقه (usul al-fiqh): The sources or foundations upon which fiqh rulings are based: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas
الكتاب (al-kitab): The Quran
السنة (al-sunnah): The prophetic traditions
الإجماع (al-ijma'): Scholarly consensus
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical deduction

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many primary sources of usul al-fiqh are mentioned in this definition?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh consists of the Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', and Qiyas, with Qiyas subsidiary to the first three.

Defining Usul al-Fiqh: Science of Rules Leading to Fiqh
A definition of usul al-fiqh and its boundaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of usul al-fiqh, identify its key components (universal rules, close attainment, verification), and distinguish it from auxiliary sciences and dialectic.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is the science of universal rules that directly lead to fiqh rulings through verification, excluding indirect sciences and polemics.

What exactly is the science of usul al-fiqh? The Hanafi tradition defines it precisely, setting boundaries that exclude other fields like grammar and dialectic. In this lesson, you will parse the definition given in al-Tawdih and al-Talwih, understanding each component and what it excludes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition's key components
Locate the three crucial elements: (1) it is knowledge of universal rules (qawa'id kulliyya), (2) it provides close attainment (tawassul qarib) to fiqh, (3) this attainment is on a basis of verification (ala wajh al-tahqiq).
These elements are explicitly stated in the first part of the passage.
2
Understand the exclusions: distant sciences
The phrase 'tawassul qarib' excludes sciences like Arabic grammar (sarf/nahw) and theology (kalam) because they do not directly lead to fiqh; they are prerequisites but not part of usul.
The passage uses 'ihtiraz' (exclusion) to mark this.
3
Understand the exclusions: dialectic and disputation
The phrase 'ala wajh al-tahqiq' excludes sciences like khilaf and jadal, which aim to compel opponents (ilzam) rather than establish truth through verification.
The text explicitly notes that such sciences are not based on tahqiq.
4
Analyze the addition of 'ilm' in the term
The commentator explains that adding 'ilm' to 'usul al-fiqh' is for extra clarification, just as one says 'shajar al-arak' (tree of arak) even though 'arak' alone suffices.
This shows the definition is meant to be emphatic and clear.
5
Define 'qa'ida' as a universal ruling
The passage defines qa'ida as a universal ruling (hukm kulli) that applies to all its particulars, from which rulings are derived when needed. Example: 'Every ruling indicated by qiyas is established.'
This completes the definition by clarifying what 'qawa'id' means.

قال المصنف في التوضيح ولما عرف أصول الفقه الا یعنی اصول فقہ کی باعتبار مرکب اضافی کے تعریف ہو چکی اب مصنف " اس کی تعریف بایں اعتبار کر رہا ہے کہ وہ علم مخصوص کا لقب ہے فیقول علم اصول الفقه النج یعنی اصول فقہ ایسے قواعد کا علم ہے جن قواعد کے ساتھ فقہ تک توصل اور وصول على وجه التحقیق ہو جائے اى العلم بالقضايا الكلية یعنی قواعد سے مراد قضایا کلیہ ہیں جن کے ساتھ فقہ کی طرف توصل قریب حاصل ہو جائے توصل کے ساتھ قریب کی قید لگا کر مباری سے احترانہ کیا ۔ كالعربية يعنى علم بالقواعد العربية كالصرف والنحوي الكلام یعنی علم الکلام ان سے توصل قریب الی الفقہ حاصل نہیں لہذا یہ اصول فقہ سے خارج ہیں۔ وقولنا على وجه التحقيق احتر از اتم یعنی علی وجہ التحقیق سے ہمارا مقصود علم الخلاف والجدل سے احتراز کرنا ہے کیونکہ یہ علم اگر چہ ایسے قواعد پشتمل ہے جو موصل الى مسائل الفقہ ہیں لیکن علی وجہ التحقیق نہیں بلکہ علی وجہ الالزام ہے اور اس سے غرض صرف الزام خصم ہوتی ہے جیسے کہ وہ قواعد جو مذکورہ فی الارشاد و المقدمہ ہیں یہ دونوں اسماء کتب ہیں صرف نکت خلافیہ کو ان پر مبتنی کیا ہے ۔
قال الشارح في التلويح قوله وعلم اصول الفقه بعد ما تقر ریعنی جب یہ متقرر اور ثابت ہو چکا ہے کہ اصول فقہ علم مخصوص کا لقب ہے تو اس وقت لفظ علم کو اصول الفقہ کی طرف مضاف کر کے علم اصول الفقہ کہنے کی ضرورت نہیں تھی بلکہ صرف اصول الفقہ کہہ دینا کافی تھا الا ان ہاں مگر یہ کہ مقصود زیادہ بیان اور زیادہ توضیح ہو تو اس وضاحت کی خاطر کہ اصول الفقہ ایک علم ہے اس لئے اصافت کر دی جیسے شجر الار اک لفظ اراک پیلو کے درخت کو کہتے ہیں لہذا شجر کے مضاف کرنے کی ضرورت نہ تھی مگر بقصد زيادة توضیح اضافت کر دی گئی ہے۔ القاعدة حکم کلی چونکہ لفظ القواعد جمع تھی للقاعدہ اس لئے قاعدہ کی تعریف کی اور کہا ایک حکم کلی جو اپنے جمیع جزئیات پر منطبق ہو اور بوقت ضرورت ان جزئیات کے احکام اس حکم کلی سے معلوم کئے جا سکیں جیسے کل حکم دل علیہ القیاس فھو ثابت اس کے ساتھ جمیع احکام قیاسی کا ثبوت حاصل ہو سکتا ہے مثلاً کہا جائے گا ہذا الحکم دل علیہ القیاس کلما
The author (Musannif) in al-Tawdih said: When he defined 'usul al-fiqh' (i.e., in terms of the compound), the definition is complete. Now the author is defining it in terms of it being a title for a specific science. He says: 'Ilm usul al-fiqh' is knowledge of rules (qawa'id) by which one attains and arrives at fiqh on a basis of verification (ala wajh al-tahqiq). That is, knowledge of universal propositions (qadaya kulliyya). Meaning: rules are universal propositions with which a close attainment (tawassul qarib) to fiqh is achieved. By adding 'close' to attainment, he excludes [distant sciences] like Arabic grammar (al-'arabiyya): knowledge of Arabic rules such as morphology (sarf) and syntax (nahw) and theology (al-kalam). These do not provide close attainment to fiqh, so they are outside usul al-fiqh. Our saying 'on a basis of verification' is a complete exclusion: i.e., by 'ala wajh al-tahqiq' we intend to exclude the science of disputation (al-khilaf) and dialectic (al-jadal). For this science, although it contains rules that lead to fiqh matters, it is not on a basis of verification but on a basis of imposing (al-izam), and its purpose is only to compel the opponent, like the rules mentioned in al-Irshad and al-Muqaddima—these are names of books, built only on points of disagreement (nukat khilafiyya). The commentator (Sharh) in al-Talwih said: His saying 'wa 'ilmu usuli al-fiqh' after it has been established. That is, when it is established that usul al-fiqh is a title for a specific science, then there was no need to add the word 'ilm' to usul al-fiqh; rather it was sufficient to say 'usul al-fiqh'. However, if the purpose is further elaboration and clarification, then for that clarification, he added the idafa, just as one says 'shajar al-arak'—the word 'arak' itself refers to the tree like a willow, so there was no need to add 'shajar', but for added clarification it is annexed. Al-qa'ida is a universal ruling; since the word 'qawa'id' is plural of qa'ida, he defined qa'ida: 'a universal ruling that applies to all its particulars and from which the rulings of those particulars can be known in times of need.' For example: 'Every ruling that is indicated by qiyas is established'—by this universal, the establishment of all qiyas rulings can be obtained. For instance, it will be said: 'This ruling is indicated by qiyas in every...'
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage provides the definition of 'Ilm Usul al-Fiqh' as a distinct field of knowledge. The definition specifies that it is knowledge of universal rules (qawa'id) that allow one to attain fiqh rulings through a process of close derivation (tawassul qarib) and on a basis of verification (ala wajh al-tahqiq). The commentary clarifies what this definition excludes: first, distant sciences like Arabic grammar and theology, which do not directly lead to fiqh; second, the science of disputation (khilaf) and dialectic (jadal), which aim to compel opponents rather than establish truth. The author then explains why the word 'ilm' (knowledge) is added to 'usul al-fiqh'—it is for emphasis and clarity, just as one might say 'tree of al-arak' even though 'arak' alone suffices. Finally, the definition of 'qa'ida' (rule) is given: a universal proposition that applies to all its particulars, from which individual rulings can be derived. An example is given: 'Every ruling indicated by qiyas is established'—this universal rule allows one to confirm any qiyas-based ruling.

Key Terms
اصول الفقه (usul al-fiqh): The science of universal rules by which fiqh rulings are derived on a basis of verification.
قواعد (qawa'id): Universal propositions (qadaya kulliyya) that apply to all their particulars and enable derivation of fiqh rulings.
توصل قریب (tawassul qarib): Close attainment, i.e., the rules directly lead to fiqh rulings, unlike distant sciences (like grammar) that are prerequisites.
علی وجہ التحقیق ('ala wajh al-tahqiq): On a basis of verification, meaning the derivation is certain and truth-seeking, as opposed to mere disputation (jadal) which aims to compel opponents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of adding the phrase 'on a basis of verification' (ala wajh al-tahqiq) in the definition of usul al-fiqh?
A) To exclude Arabic grammar and theology from usul al-fiqh.
B) To exclude the science of disputation (khilaf) and dialectic (jadal).
C) To emphasize that the rules must be universal.
D) To indicate that usul al-fiqh is a science of certain knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is the science of universal rules that directly lead to fiqh rulings through verification, excluding indirect sciences and polemical dialectic.

Method of Learning
intermediate
8 min
Near and Distant Means to Fiqh
Classifies means to fiqh as near or distant.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between tawassul qarib and tawassul ba'id, and explain why Arabic grammar and kalam are classified as distant means.

Core Idea
The direct path to fiqh is usul al-fiqh; Arabic grammar and kalam are distant stepping stones.

This passage from al-Tawdih explains the definition of fiqh and the means to acquire it. It clarifies that not all tools that help in deriving rulings are themselves part of fiqh; some are preparatory sciences. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for a student of usul to prioritize studies correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of tawassul
Locate the terms 'tawassul qarib' (near means) and 'tawassul ba'id' (distant means) in the passage. Understand that the passage is classifying the paths to fiqh.
The classification is based on directness: near means directly yield fiqh; distant means yield an intermediary.
2
Understand the causality relation
The passage states that the 'near' condition is derived from causality. A near cause directly produces its effect; a distant cause produces an intermediary that then becomes the near cause.
Example: fire directly produces heat (near cause), while the sun heats the earth through radiation (distant cause).
3
Apply the rule to exclude Arabic and kalam
Arabic grammar gives knowledge of word indications, and kalam gives affirmation of the sources. Both are intermediaries that enable usul al-fiqh to then derive rulings. Therefore, they are not near means.
The passage explicitly says 'they are principles for usul al-fiqh, not direct means to fiqh'.
4
Explain why they are classified as distant
Because through Arabic grammar we attain knowledge of how words indicate meanings, and through kalam we affirm the authority of Quran and Sunnah. Only after these can usul al-fiqh operate to derive rulings. Hence, the path is longer.
This distinction helps students of fiqh understand the prerequisite sciences.

دل علیہ القیاس فھو ثابت تو نتیجہ ہو گا ہذا الحکم ثابت و التوصل القريب مستفاد یعنی توصل کے ساتھ جو قریب کی قید لگائی ہے وہ بجھا کی بار سببیت سے مستفاد ہے جو سببیہ قریبہ میں ظاہر و متبادر ہے دوسرا توصل الی الفقہ سے کیونکہ سبب قریب ہی موصل الی الفقہ ہوتا ہے اور سبب بعید موصل الى الواسطہ ہوتا ہے اور یہی واسطہ سبب قریب ہو کہ موصل الی الفقہ ہوتا ہے ۔ فيخرج العلم بقواعد العربية سببية قریبہ کے ساتھ علم بقواعد العربیہ و قواعد الکلام خارج ہو جائیں گے کیونکہ یہ دونوں مبادی ہیں برائے اصول فقہ اور ان کے ساتھ توصل الی الفقہ توصل قریب نہیں ہے کیونکہ قواعد عربیہ کے ساتھ توصل ہوتا ہے الى معرفة كيفية دلالة الالفاظ یعنی ان قواعد سے یہ حاصل ہوتا ہے کہ الفاظ کی دلالت علی مدلولاتها الوضعیہ کس قسم کی دلالت ہے مطابقی ہے یا تضمنی والتزامی اور پھر یہ دلالت علی سبیل الفا علیہ ہے یا علی سبیل المفعولية وغيرها - وبواسطة ذلك اور اسی کے واسطہ سے اقتدار علی استنباط الاحكام من الكتاب والسنة حاصل ہوتا - وكذا لك يتوصل بقواعد الکلام یعنی علم الکلام کے قواعد سے توصل الى ثبوت الكتاب والسنة حاصل ہوتا ہے یعنی ان قواعد کلامیہ سے کتاب اللہ کا کتاب اللہ ہونا اور سنہ کا سنتہ رسول ہونا اور ان کے صدق کا وجوب حاصل ہوتا جو علم الکلام کے مطابق عقائد نہیں رکھتا تو وہ کتاب اللہ کو اور سنہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کو تسلیم نہیں کرے گا اور نہ ان کے صدق کا قائل ہو گا تو علم الکلام سے ان کا ثبوت حاصل ہوا پھر اس کے بعد ان کے ذریعہ توصل الی الفقہ ہوگا تو یہ توصل قریب نہ ہوا بلکہ بعید ہوا و التحقيق في هذا المقامرال حاصل تحقیق یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے انسان کو عبث اور سری یعنی مہمل پیدا نہیں فرمایا کہ اس کے اعمال و افعال کے ساتھ کوئی حکم تعلق نہ پکڑے بلکہ انسان کے ہر اعمال کے ساتھ شارع کی جانب سے کوئی نہ کوئی حکم از قسم وجوب و ندب حرمت و کراہتہ وغیرہ میں سے تعلق پکڑنا ہے اور یہ حکم معلق اور وابستہ ہوتا ہے اپنی مخصوص دلیل کے ساتھ تاکہ اس سے بوقت حاجت کے استنباط کیا جائے اور اس حکم پر اس کے مناسبات کو قیاس کیا جا سکے اس پر یہ اشکال وارد ہوتا ہے کہ جب انسان کے ہر عمل کے ساتھ شارع کی جانب سے کوئی نہ کوئی حکم متعلق ہے اور اپنی دلیل کے ساتھ وابستہ ہے تو جمیع احکام حاصل ہو گئے تو پھر لیستنبط ویقاس کی کیا ضرورت ہے تو اس اشکال کا ایک جواب تو یہ دیا گیا ہے کہ عبارت میں تقدیر ہے اور لیستنبط تعلیل لمقدر اصل یوں ہے صرح ببعض ذلك الحكم يستنبط عند الحاجة من دليله و يقاس علی ذلک المصرح به مايناسبه - دوسرا جواب اس کا یہ ہے کہ بنائے اشکال یہ ہے کہ اس عبارت سے یہ وہم کیا گیا ہے کہ جمیع احکام کا حصول بالفعل مراد ہے حالانکہ یوں نہیں بلکہ مراد یہ ہے کہ شارع کی جانب سے انسان کے ہر عمل کے ساتھ نفس الامر میں کوئی نہ کوئی حکم متعلق ضرور ہے جو اپنی دلیل مخصوص از قسم نص و اجماع کے ساتھ وابستہ ہے تا کہ جب حاجت پیش آئے تو فقیہہ ان احکام کو ان دلائل ثلثہ کتاب ، سنت اور اجماع سے اخذ کر سکے اگر ان اصول ثلثہ میں نہ ملے تو پھر ان کو مناسبات پر قیاس کر کے حاصل کر سکے اور اس مراد پر کوئی اشکال وارد نہیں ہو سکتا۔ لتعذر الاحاطة یہ علہ ہے ويقاس على ذلك ما يناسبہ کی حاصل یہ ہے کہ تمام احکام الی یوم القیام کے بصورت منصوص ہونے کے موجود اور حاصل نہیں ہو سکتے تھے لتعذر الاحاطة بجميع الجزئيات اس لئے ایک اصول شریعہ قیاس کو قرار دیا گیا تا کہ بوقت ضرورت یہ مسائل قیاسیہ حاصل ہوسکیں۔ فحصلت قضایا موضوعاتها الم یہ تفریح ہے علی قولہ ان الانسان لم يخلق عبدا الم یعنی جب انسان کے ہر عمل اور فعل کے ساتھ کوئی نہ کوئی حکم از جانب شارع متعلق ہے تو اس صورت میں ایسے قضایا حاصل ہوئے جن کے موضوع افعال مکلفین ہوئے اور محمول احكام شارع على التفصيل مثلاً الصلواة واجبة - الحج واجب النه نا حرام و غیر با قسمى الغلوبها اى باحكام الشارع الحاصل من تلك الادلة یہ صفت علم ہے یعنی ایسا علم بالاحکام جو حاصل من الادلہ ہے اس کا نام فقہ رکھا گیا تو نظروا في تفاصيل الادلة النج یہ اصول فقہ کی ضرورت کے لئے تمہید اور وجہ احتیاج ہے یعنی پھر علماء نے اولہ اور احکام کے تفصیلات کی طرف نظر والتفات کی اور انہیں خصوص سے عموم کی طرف لے گئے تو تمام ادلہ تفصیلیہ کا رجوع الى الكتاب والسنة والإجماع والقیاس انہوں نے پایا اور احکام کار جوع الى الوجوب والندب و الاباحة والحرمة والكراتة و تأملوا اور انہوں نے غور فرمایا کہ ان ادلہ کے ساتھ ان احکام پر طریق استدلال کیسے ہو اور اس کی کیفیت کیا ہوگی اور یہ نگاہ اجمالاً تھی اور تفصیلی احکام اور تفصیلی ادلہ کی طرف ان کی توجہ نہیں تھی الا یہ کہ کہیں مثال کے طور پر تفصیلی دلیل ذکر کر دیں تو اور بات ہے مثلاً کہا جائے گا الامر للوجوب اور شریعت میں جتنی او امر احکام ہیں ان کی تفصیل پیش نہیں کی جائے گی مگر بطور مثال کے مثلاً یوں کہ دیں کہ صلوۃ واجب ہے کیونکہ اس کے لئے اللہ تعالیٰ کا امرا قیموا الصلوۃ وارد ہے تو یہ تفصیل بطور مثال کے ہے۔ فحصل لهم قضايا كلية الہم یعنی اس نظر و تامل کے بعد ان کے لئے کچھ قضایا کلیہ حاصل ہوئے جو ان احکام پر ان ادر کے ساتھ اجمالاً استدلال کرنے کی کیفیت کے ساتھ متعلق تھے اور بیان طرق اور بیان شرائط بھی کیا گیا اور ان قضایا میں سے ہر ایک قضیہ وقانون کے ساتھ بہت سے
If qiyas indicates it, then the conclusion is: this ruling is proven. And the near means (al-tawassul al-qarib) is derived from {؟}, i.e., the condition of 'near' attached to tawassul is derived from causality, which is apparent and obvious in near causality. The second is tawassul to fiqh, because only the near cause leads to fiqh, while the distant cause leads to an intermediary, and this intermediary becomes a near cause that leads to fiqh. Thus, knowledge of Arabic grammar and rhetoric are excluded from near causality, because both are principles for usul al-fiqh, and with them tawassul to fiqh is not near, because through Arabic grammar we attain knowledge of how words indicate their conventional meanings—whether it is mutabaqah, tadhammun, iltizam, and whether the indication is by way of wad' al-alfiyyah or by way of maf'uliyyah, etc. Through that, ability to derive rulings from the Book and Sunnah is attained. Similarly, through the principles of kalam (theology) we attain the affirmation of the Book and Sunnah—that the Book of Allah is the Book of Allah and the Sunnah is the Sunnah of the Messenger, and the obligation of their truth is attained. Whoever does not hold correct beliefs according to kalam will not accept the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of the Messenger, nor will he affirm their truth. Thus, through kalam their affirmation is attained, then afterwards tawassul to fiqh occurs. So this tawassul is not near but distant. The verification in this discussion: The result is that Allah did not create man in vain or aimlessly such that no ruling is attached to his actions. Rather, every action of man has some ruling from the Lawgiver—obligation, recommendation, prohibition, dislike, etc.—attached to it. This ruling is suspended and connected to its specific evidence so that it can be derived from it at the time of need, and qiyas can be made upon it for its parallels. Upon this, an objection arises: If every action has a ruling attached to it and is connected to its evidence, then all rulings are already obtained, so what need is there for 'so that they derive and perform qiyas'? One answer given is that there is a suppressed phrase in the text, and 'li yastanbit' is a cause for the suppressed part, the original being: 'He explicitly stated some of that ruling to be derived when needed from its evidence, and upon that explicitly stated ruling qiyas is made to what is parallel to it.' The second answer is that the objection is based on imagining that 'all rulings are actually obtained' is intended, but it is not. Rather, the intention is that in reality, every action of man has some ruling from the Lawgiver attached to it, which is connected to its specific evidence—whether text or consensus—so that when need arises, the jurist can extract these rulings from those three sources: Book, Sunnah, and Ijma. If not found in those three principles, then he can obtain them through qiyas on the parallels. No objection can be raised against this meaning. 'Because of the impossibility of encompassing' is the cause for saying 'and qiyas upon that what is appropriate to it'. The result is that all rulings until the Day of Judgment cannot exist and be obtained in the form of being explicitly stated, due to the impossibility of encompassing all particulars. Therefore, qiyas was established as a principle of Shari'ah so that when needed, these qiyasi issues may be obtained. Thus, there resulted propositions whose subjects are the actions of the mukallaf and whose predicates are the rulings of the Shari'ah in detail, e.g., prayer is obligatory, Hajj is obligatory, wine is forbidden, and other categories of Shari'ah rulings obtained from those evidences. This attribute of knowledge—that is, such knowledge of rulings obtained from evidences—is called fiqh. Then they looked into the details of the evidences. This is a prelude and reason for the need for usul al-fiqh. That is, scholars looked into the details of rulings and evidences and moved from particulars to generals. They found that all detailed evidences refer to the Book, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas, and rulings refer to obligation, recommendation, permission, prohibition, and dislike. They pondered how the method of inference from these evidences for these rulings is, and what its quality is. This was a general view; they did not focus on detailed rulings and detailed evidences except if they mentioned a detailed evidence as an example—e.g., it is said 'the command indicates obligation', and they would not present the detailed commands in Shari'ah except as an example, like saying 'prayer is obligatory because the command of Allah 'establish prayer' has come'. So this detail is by way of example. Thus, general propositions (qadaya kulliyya) were obtained for them, which pertain to the quality of inference from those evidences in a general way, and the methods and conditions were also stated. Each of these propositions, along with its rule, [applies to] many...
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a discussion from al-Tawdih regarding the definition of fiqh and the need for usul al-fiqh. The commentator explains the distinction between near (qarib) and distant (ba'id) means (tawassul) to fiqh. Near means directly lead to fiqh, like the science of usul al-fiqh itself. Distant means, such as Arabic grammar (to understand word indications) and kalam (to affirm the authority of Quran and Sunnah), are preparatory and do not directly yield fiqh rulings. The passage then addresses an objection: if every action has a Shari'ah ruling attached to its evidence, then all rulings are already known, so why is ijtihad and qiyas needed? The author responds by clarifying that rulings are not all explicitly detailed; rather, they are in principle connected to their sources, and the jurist must derive them when needed. Since it is impossible to explicitly state every ruling for all particulars, qiyas was established as a fourth source. The scholars then, by examining the four sources (Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) and the categories of rulings (wajib, mandub, mubah, haram, makruh), derived general principles (qadaya kulliyya) that form the substance of usul al-fiqh. These principles are not concerned with specific rulings (e.g., 'prayer is obligatory') except as examples; rather, they deal with the general methods of inference and conditions.

Key Terms
التوصل القريب (al-tawassul al-qarib): The direct means to attain fiqh, i.e., usul al-fiqh itself.
التوصل البعيد (al-tawassul al-ba'id): Indirect means to fiqh through an intermediary, such as Arabic grammar or kalam.
الاستنباط (al-istinbat): Derivation of rulings from their evidences (Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main difference between tawassul qarib and tawassul ba'id, according to the passage?
A) Tawassul qarib is through qiyas, while tawassul ba'id is through ijma.
B) Tawassul qarib directly yields fiqh (like usul al-fiqh), while tawassul ba'id yields an intermediary (like Arabic grammar) that then leads to fiqh.
C) Tawassul qarib is for scholars, while tawassul ba'id is for laymen.
D) Tawassul qarib is from Quran and Sunnah, while tawassul ba'id is from analogy.

Key Takeaway
The direct path to fiqh is usul al-fiqh; Arabic grammar and kalam are preparatory distant means.

Method of Learning
intermediate

The Necessity of Qiyas and the Genesis of Usul al-Fiqh
Addresses an objection about the need for qiyas and describes the derivation of usul al-fiqh principles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to refute the objection that if all rulings are attached to actions, no ijtihad is needed, and explain how usul al-fiqh was derived from detailed evidences.

Core Idea
The impossibility of enumerating all particulars requires qiyas; usul al-fiqh provides the general principles for derivation.

After establishing that every action has a ruling connected to its evidence, the author anticipates a critical objection: if all rulings are already there, why is ijtihad needed? The answer reveals the foundational role of qiyas and the process by which scholars distilled usul al-fiqh from the four sources. This lesson unpacks that objection and its resolution.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the objection
The passage states an objection: if every action of a human has a ruling from the Lawgiver attached to its evidence, then all rulings are already obtained. So why do we need to 'derive' (yastanbit) and 'perform qiyas' (yuqas)?
This objection assumes that 'having a ruling attached' means the ruling is explicitly known.
2
Analyze the first answer
The first answer says the phrase 'li yastanbit' (to derive) is a cause for a suppressed part: that some rulings are explicitly stated so they can be derived when needed, and qiyas is made on those explicit rulings for parallels.
This answer implies that not all rulings are explicitly stated; only some are given as examples.
3
Analyze the second answer
The second answer clarifies that the objection is based on a misunderstanding: the passage does not mean that all rulings are obtained in actuality; rather, it means that in reality (fi nafs al-amr) every action has a ruling attached to its specific evidence (text or consensus), and the jurist must extract it when needed. If not found in those three sources, qiyas on parallels is used.
The key phrase: 'لتعذر الاحاطة بجميع الجزئيات' (due to the impossibility of encompassing all particulars).
4
Understand the role of qiyas
Because it is impossible to explicitly state every ruling for every particular event until the Day of Judgment, qiyas was established as a principle of Shari'ah. Thus, qiyas is not a substitute but a necessary extension.
This shows that qiyas is based on the principle of completeness of Shari'ah.
5
Trace the derivation of usul al-fiqh
Scholars looked into detailed rulings and evidences and derived general propositions (qadaya kulliyya) that cover the methods and conditions of inference. These propositions are the subject of usul al-fiqh.
The passage gives examples: 'al-amr li al-wujub' (the command indicates obligation).

If qiyas indicates it, then the conclusion is: this ruling is proven. And the near means (al-tawassul al-qarib) is derived from {؟}, i.e., the condition of 'near' attached to tawassul is derived from causality, which is apparent and obvious in near causality. The second is tawassul to fiqh, because only the near cause leads to fiqh, while the distant cause leads to an intermediary, and this intermediary becomes a near cause that leads to fiqh. Thus, knowledge of Arabic grammar and rhetoric are excluded from near causality, because both are principles for usul al-fiqh, and with them tawassul to fiqh is not near, because through Arabic grammar we attain knowledge of how words indicate their conventional meanings—whether it is mutabaqah, tadhammun, iltizam, and whether the indication is by way of wad' al-alfiyyah or by way of maf'uliyyah, etc. Through that, ability to derive rulings from the Book and Sunnah is attained. Similarly, through the principles of kalam (theology) we attain the affirmation of the Book and Sunnah—that the Book of Allah is the Book of Allah and the Sunnah is the Sunnah of the Messenger, and the obligation of their truth is attained. Whoever does not hold correct beliefs according to kalam will not accept the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of the Messenger, nor will he affirm their truth. Thus, through kalam their affirmation is attained, then afterwards tawassul to fiqh occurs. So this tawassul is not near but distant. The verification in this discussion: The result is that Allah did not create man in vain or aimlessly such that no ruling is attached to his actions. Rather, every action of man has some ruling from the Lawgiver—obligation, recommendation, prohibition, dislike, etc.—attached to it. This ruling is suspended and connected to its specific evidence so that it can be derived from it at the time of need, and qiyas can be made upon it for its parallels. Upon this, an objection arises: If every action has a ruling attached to it and is connected to its evidence, then all rulings are already obtained, so what need is there for 'so that they derive and perform qiyas'? One answer given is that there is a suppressed phrase in the text, and 'li yastanbit' is a cause for the suppressed part, the original being: 'He explicitly stated some of that ruling to be derived when needed from its evidence, and upon that explicitly stated ruling qiyas is made to what is parallel to it.' The second answer is that the objection is based on imagining that 'all rulings are actually obtained' is intended, but it is not. Rather, the intention is that in reality, every action of man has some ruling from the Lawgiver attached to it, which is connected to its specific evidence—whether text or consensus—so that when need arises, the jurist can extract these rulings from those three sources: Book, Sunnah, and Ijma. If not found in those three principles, then he can obtain them through qiyas on the parallels. No objection can be raised against this meaning. 'Because of the impossibility of encompassing' is the cause for saying 'and qiyas upon that what is appropriate to it'. The result is that all rulings until the Day of Judgment cannot exist and be obtained in the form of being explicitly stated, due to the impossibility of encompassing all particulars. Therefore, qiyas was established as a principle of Shari'ah so that when needed, these qiyasi issues may be obtained. Thus, there resulted propositions whose subjects are the actions of the mukallaf and whose predicates are the rulings of the Shari'ah in detail, e.g., prayer is obligatory, Hajj is obligatory, wine is forbidden, and other categories of Shari'ah rulings obtained from those evidences. This attribute of knowledge—that is, such knowledge of rulings obtained from evidences—is called fiqh. Then they looked into the details of the evidences. This is a prelude and reason for the need for usul al-fiqh. That is, scholars looked into the details of rulings and evidences and moved from particulars to generals. They found that all detailed evidences refer to the Book, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas, and rulings refer to obligation, recommendation, permission, prohibition, and dislike. They pondered how the method of inference from these evidences for these rulings is, and what its quality is. This was a general view; they did not focus on detailed rulings and detailed evidences except if they mentioned a detailed evidence as an example—e.g., it is said 'the command indicates obligation', and they would not present the detailed commands in Shari'ah except as an example, like saying 'prayer is obligatory because the command of Allah 'establish prayer' has come'. So this detail is by way of example. Thus, general propositions (qadaya kulliyya) were obtained for them, which pertain to the quality of inference from those evidences in a general way, and the methods and conditions were also stated. Each of these propositions, along with its rule, [applies to] many...

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a discussion from al-Tawdih regarding the definition of fiqh and the need for usul al-fiqh. The commentator explains the distinction between near (qarib) and distant (ba'id) means (tawassul) to fiqh. Near means directly lead to fiqh, like the science of usul al-fiqh itself. Distant means, such as Arabic grammar (to understand word indications) and kalam (to affirm the authority of Quran and Sunnah), are preparatory and do not directly yield fiqh rulings. The passage then addresses an objection: if every action has a Shari'ah ruling attached to its evidence, then all rulings are already known, so why is ijtihad and qiyas needed? The author responds by clarifying that rulings are not all explicitly detailed; rather, they are in principle connected to their sources, and the jurist must derive them when needed. Since it is impossible to explicitly state every ruling for all particulars, qiyas was established as a fourth source. The scholars then, by examining the four sources (Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) and the categories of rulings (wajib, mandub, mubah, haram, makruh), derived general principles (qadaya kulliyya) that form the substance of usul al-fiqh. These principles are not concerned with specific rulings (e.g., 'prayer is obligatory') except as examples; rather, they deal with the general methods of inference and conditions.

Key Terms
التوصل القريب (al-tawassul al-qarib): The direct means to attain fiqh, i.e., usul al-fiqh itself.
التوصل البعيد (al-tawassul al-ba'id): Indirect means to fiqh through an intermediary, such as Arabic grammar or kalam.
الاستنباط (al-istinbat): Derivation of rulings from their evidences (Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas).
القضايا الكلية (al-qadaya al-kulliyya): General propositions that form the subject matter of usul al-fiqh, e.g., 'al-amr li al-wujub'.

Key Takeaway

The Syllogistic Structure of Fiqh Reasoning
Explains the logical form of fiqh deduction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a conjunctive syllogism (qiyas iqtirani) to derive a fiqh ruling from a universal usul principle.

Core Idea
Fiqh rulings are derived by applying universal usul premises to specific acts via syllogism.

Fiqh reasoning often follows a logical pattern: you start with a general rule from usul al-fiqh (the major premise) and apply it to a specific act (the minor premise) to reach a conclusion. This passage explains the four figures of the conjunctive syllogism and shows how the example of Hajj being obligatory is derived. Understanding this structure is key to seeing how usul al-fiqh functions as the methodology for deducing rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its desired ruling
Determine which specific action (e.g., Hajj) you want the ruling for. This will be the subject (minor term) of the conclusion.
The desired ruling is the predicate (major term) in the conclusion.
2
Recall the relevant universal principle from usul
Identify a universal proposition (qadiyya kulliyya) from usul al-fiqh that covers acts of this type. For example, 'Everything commanded by the Lawgiver is obligatory.' This will be the major premise (kubra).
These principles are derived from Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas.
3
Form the minor premise by linking the act to the middle term
Take the act (e.g., Hajj) and affirm that it falls under the condition stated in the universal principle. For example, 'Hajj is commanded by the Lawgiver.' This is the minor premise (sughra).
The middle term (awsat) is the common element: 'commanded by the Lawgiver.'
4
Arrange the premises in the correct figure
Place the middle term in its proper position. In the first figure (most common), the middle term is predicate in the minor premise and subject in the major premise.
Other figures (second, third, fourth) are less common in fiqh reasoning.
5
Derive the conclusion
The conclusion follows necessarily: the act (minor term) receives the ruling (major term). For Hajj: 'Hajj is obligatory.' This is the fiqh ruling.
The conclusion is implicit in the premises; the syllogism makes it explicit.

مقدموں سے مرکب ہوتی ہے ان میں سے ایک مقدمہ مشتمل علی الاصغر ہوتا ہے اسے صغریٰ کہتے ہیں دوسرا مشتمل علی الاکبر ہوتا ہے اسے کبری کہتے ہیں اور یہ دونوں مقدمے ایک امر متکرر پشتمل ہوتے ہیں اسے اوسط کہتے ہیں یہ صدا وسط اگر جمول فی الصغری اور موضوع فی الکبری ہو توا سے شکل اول کہتے ہیں اگر اس کے برعکس ہو تو شکل رابع اگر حد وسط دونوں میں محمول ہو تو شکل ثانی اگر دونوں میں موضوع ہو تو شکل ثالث کہلاتی ہے۔ مثلا اذا قلنا الحج واجب اور اس پر دلیل پیش کرتے ہوئے کہا جائے۔ لانے ما مور الشارع وكل ما صور الشارع فهو واجب تو نتیجہ آئے گا الحج واجب ۔ اس میں الحج اصغر ہے اور لفظ واجب اکبر ہے اور لفظ مامور الشارع اوسط ہے اور الجی مامور الشارع صغری ہے اور کل مأمور الشارع واجب کبری اور یہ دلیل شکل اول کی صورت پر ہے کیونکہ صدا وسط محمول فی الصغری اور موضوع فی الکبریٰ ہے۔ فالقواعد التي يتوصل اج اور قواعد اصولیہ جن کے ساتھ فقہ کی طرف وصول ہوتا گیہی وہ قضایا کلیہ ہیں جو کبری بنتے ہیں صغری کے لئے جو سہل الحصول ہوتا ہے جس عمل وفعل کا حکم جاننا چاہتے ہیں اس کو موضوع بنائیے اور قضیہ کلیہ کے موضوع کو اس کے لئے محمول بناتے تو صغریٰ حاصل ہو جائے گا مثلاً حج کا حکم جاننا چاہتے ہیں تو لفظ الج کو موضوع بنائیے اور اصول فقہ کا جو قضیہ کلیہ ہے کہ کل مامور الشارع واجب اس میں سے اس کا موضوع مامور الشارع کو الجے کے لئے محمول بنائیے تو ہو جائے گا الج مامور الشارع یہ ہو اصغری اور قضیہ کلیہ کو اس کے کبری بنائیے جو نتیجہ ہوگا وہ مطلوبہ حکم ہوگا تو اس صورت میں مطلوب فقی بالقوہ سے نکل کر بالفعل کی طرف آجائے گا یہی مراد ہے توصل إلى الفقه كي لكن تحصيل القاعدة الخ لیکن اس قاعدہ کلیہ کا حاصل کرنا موقوف ہے احوال ادلہ اور احکام کی بحث پر اور ان کے شرائط و قیود کی تبیین پر جو قاعدہ کے کلیہ ہونے میں معتبر اور ضروری ہیں اور جو مباحث ان امور کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں یہ تمام اصول فقہ کے مطالب ہیں جو علم بالقاعدۃ الکلیہ کے تحت درج ہیں علی ما شرحہ المصنف بمالا مزید علیہ شارج نے یہ دلیل اقترانی کی تفصیل کی ہے مسائل فقہیہ میں بالعموم یہی جاری ہوتی ہے اور قیاس استثنائی کا ذکر نہیں کیونکہ وہ قلیل الاستعمال ہے ۔
It is composed of propositions; among them one proposition contains the minor term, it is called the minor (sughra), the second contains the major term, it is called the major (kubra), and both these propositions contain a shared term called the middle (awsat). If this middle term is a predicate in the minor and a subject in the major, it is called the first figure; if the opposite, the fourth figure; if the middle is a predicate in both, the second figure; if subject in both, the third figure. For example, when we say 'Hajj is obligatory' and present a proof: 'Because (the command of the Lawgiver) and everything commanded by the Lawgiver is obligatory.' Then the conclusion will be 'Hajj is obligatory.' In this, 'Hajj' is the minor, 'obligatory' is the major, and 'commanded by the Lawgiver' is the middle. 'Hajj is commanded by the Lawgiver' is the minor premise, and 'Everything commanded by the Lawgiver is obligatory' is the major premise. This proof is in the first figure because the middle term is predicate in the minor and subject in the major. The usul al-fiqh principles by which one reaches fiqh are universal propositions that serve as major premises for the minor premises which are easily obtained. When you want to know the ruling of an action, make that action the subject, and make the subject of the universal proposition its predicate, then the minor premise is obtained. For example, to know the ruling of Hajj, make the word 'Hajj' the subject, and from the universal proposition of usul al-fiqh 'Everything commanded by the Lawgiver is obligatory', take its subject 'commanded by the Lawgiver' and make it the predicate for 'Hajj', resulting in 'Hajj is commanded by the Lawgiver' as the minor premise, and the universal proposition as the major premise; the resulting conclusion is the sought ruling. In this way, the desired ruling becomes actualized from potential. This is the meaning of 'tawassul ila al-fiqh' (attaining fiqh). But obtaining this universal rule depends on the discussion of the states of proofs and rulings, and on the clarification of their conditions and restrictions that are essential for the rule to be universal. The discussions related to these matters are all the subjects of usul al-fiqh, which fall under the knowledge of the universal rule (al-qa'ida al-kulliyya), as the author (Sadr al-Shariah) explained comprehensively. The commentator (sharih) has detailed this conjunctive syllogism (qiyas iqtirani); it is generally used in fiqhi issues, and the exceptional syllogism (qiyas istithna'i) is not mentioned because it is rarely used.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is from a commentary on al-Tawdih, explaining the logical structure of fiqh reasoning. It describes the four figures of the Aristotelian syllogism (qiyas iqtirani) and applies it to the example of Hajj being obligatory. The key point is that usul al-fiqh consists of universal propositions (qadaya kulliyya) that serve as the major premise in a syllogism; the specific act under consideration becomes the minor premise, and the conclusion is the fiqh ruling. This is the method of 'tawassul' (attaining) fiqh. The passage then notes that obtaining these universal rules requires studying the conditions and qualifications of proofs and rulings, which are the very topics of usul al-fiqh. The author states that the conjunctive syllogism is commonly used in fiqh, not the exceptional syllogism. The commentator (the author of this sharh) expands on this by explaining how to construct the syllogism: take the act whose ruling you seek as the subject, and then use the universal rule from usul to form the minor premise. For example, using the rule 'Everything commanded by the Lawgiver is obligatory' (a major premise), you derive that 'Hajj is commanded by the Lawgiver' (minor) to conclude 'Hajj is obligatory' (conclusion). This demonstrates the role of usul al-fiqh as the tool for deriving fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
صغریٰ (sughra): The minor premise in a syllogism, which contains the subject of the conclusion.
کبریٰ (kubra): The major premise in a syllogism, which contains the predicate of the conclusion.
اوسط (awsat): The middle term that appears in both premises but not in the conclusion.
قضیہ کلیہ (qadiyya kulliyya): A universal proposition that serves as a major premise in fiqh reasoning; these are the rules of usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example given (Hajj), what is the middle term (awsat) in the syllogism?
A) Hajj
B) Obligatory
C) Commanded by the Lawgiver
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
Fiqh rulings are deduced by applying universal usul principles (major premise) to specific acts (minor premise) through a conjunctive syllogism, typically in the first figure.
