سوم ادب تھا ۔ فلمن اختار النظم اسی وجہ سے نظم کو بجائے لفظ کے اختیار کیا وقد روی عن ابي حنيفة الخ امام ابو حنیفہ کی اس روایت مذکورہ سے یہ وہم ہوتا تھا کہ قرآن مجید صرف معنی کا نام ہے اور نظم و عبارت کو اس میں دخل نہیں ہے اس لئے اس روایت کی وضات کردی اور کہا کہ امام کے نزدیک صرف جواز صلوۃ کے بارہ میں نظم رکن لازمی نہیں ہے
The author said in al-Tawdih: 'We will present its discussions' i.e., the discussions of the book, between them: first, on it conveying meaning. Know that the main purpose of the Book of Allah is conveying a legal ruling, but conveying a legal ruling depends on the composition (nazm) conveying meaning. So after understanding the meaning, the ruling can be known. Therefore, research is necessary, i.e., research regarding the Book of Allah being meaningful. So the first chapter is about the discussion of conveying meaning. In this chapter, discussions of specific, general, shared, real, metaphorical, etc., will be conducted in terms of them conveying meaning. And the second chapter is on it conveying legal ruling. In the second chapter, the discussion will be regarding the Book of Allah conveying a legal ruling. So the discussion of command (amr) will be in terms of it conveying obligation (wujub), and prohibition (nahy) in terms of it necessitating prohibition (hurma), and obligation and prohibition are legal rulings. The commentator said: his statement 'we will present its discussions' means we will explain its types and the conditions that are related to conveying meanings and establishing rulings, and what relates to the definition of the Book is outside this topic. And by 'discussions' are meant discussions related to conveying meanings that have a greater connection with conveying rulings, and whose complete clarification has not been done in the Arabic sciences, such as particularization (khusus), generalization (umum), shared (ishtirak), etc., not like declension (i‘rab) etc. That is, declension and construction (bina), or definition and indefinition, whose discussions have been covered in the Arabic sciences. Even though they are related to conveying meaning, their discussion will not be undertaken in usul al-fiqh. It may be said: The intended meaning is that we will bring those discussions that are related to the Book of Allah being meaningful, whereas the discussions presented are not only related to the Book of Allah but also to the Sunnah. We respond: This is an accepted objection. The discussions in the first chapter and likewise the second chapter are such that they are related not only to the composition of the Book but also to the Sunnah. Therefore, it would have been proper to postpone them after both the Book and the Sunnah. But because the composition of the Book is preserved and mutawatir, and the composition of the Sunnah is not like that, these discussions are more appropriate and attached to the composition of the Book. Thus, it is mentioned after it. The author said in al-Tawdih: 'The first chapter: Since the Qur'an is composition (nazm) ...' i.e., because the noble Qur'an is a composition that indicates meaning, therefore the division of words in relation to meaning yields four divisions. In terms of meaning, composition (nazm) and word (lafz) are the same thing. However, applying the word (lafz) to the noble Qur'an involves a kind of impropriety because the lexical meaning of lafz is 'to throw something from the mouth'. So calling the Qur'an lafz was discourteous according to this meaning. Therefore, nazm was chosen instead of lafz. And it has been narrated from Abu Hanifa... From this mentioned narration, it was misunderstood that the noble Qur'an is only meaning and composition and expression have no part in it. Therefore, he clarified the narration and said that according to the Imam, only regarding the permissibility of prayer, composition is not an essential pillar.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage explains the structure of the book (al-Tawdih). The author states that the primary purpose of the Quran is to convey legal rulings, but that depends on the composition conveying meaning. Hence, the book has two chapters: Chapter One discusses how the Quran conveys meaning (topics like specific, general, shared, real, metaphorical), and Chapter Two discusses how it conveys legal rulings (e.g., command indicates obligation, prohibition indicates prohibition). The commentator clarifies that discussions of Arabic grammar (i‘rab, definition) are excluded as they are covered in Arabic sciences. An objection is raised: these discussions apply to both Quran and Sunnah, so why attach them only to the Quran? The response is that the Quran's composition is preserved and mutawatir, while the Sunnah's composition is not, making the discussions more fitting for the Quran. Finally, the passage explains why the term 'nazm' (composition) is used rather than 'lafz' (word), because 'lafz' literally means 'to throw from the mouth', which is improper for the Quran. A narration from Abu Hanifa is referenced and clarified to show that he did not deny the importance of composition entirely, but only regarding the permissibility of prayer.

Key Terms
نظم (nazm): Composition or structure of words that conveys meaning; preferred term for the Quran over 'lafz' due to respect.
لفظ (lafz): Word, lexically meaning 'to throw from the mouth'; considered somewhat disrespectful for the Quran.
إفادة المعنى (ifadat al-ma'na): Conveying meaning; the topic of the first chapter of the book.
إفادة الحكم الشرعي (ifadat al-hukm al-shar'i): Conveying a legal ruling; the topic of the second chapter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because these topics are not found in the Sunnah.
B) Because the Quran's composition is preserved and mutawatir, while the Sunnah's composition is not.
C) Because the author only wanted to discuss the Quran.
D) Because the Sunnah cannot convey general or specific meanings.

Key Takeaway
The structure of al-Tawdih reflects the fundamental principle that legal rulings depend on understanding meaning, and the Quran's preserved composition makes it the primary text for developing these tools.

Definitions of Ada (Performance) and Qada (Making Up) and Their Metaphorical Usage
Defining ada and qada and their mutual metaphorical usage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of ada and qada, explain why 'thābit bil-amr' is used in ada's definition, and compare the two views on the cause of qada's obligation.

Core Idea
Ada is exact performance of what is commanded; qada is its substitute; both share the attribute of delivering to the deserving recipient.

This passage from a classical usul text lays out the technical definitions of two key terms: ada (performance) and qada (making up). The author carefully chooses 'thābit bil-amr' (established by command) for ada to include supererogatory acts, while qada is restricted to obligatory acts. Beyond definitions, the passage also explores a secondary legal dispute: does the obligation to make up a missed act arise from the same command that required the original performance, or does it require a new textual basis?

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Locate the Arabic terms for ada and qada and their definitions. Note the key difference: ada uses 'thābit', qada uses 'wājib'.
2
Analyze the inclusion of nawafil
Explain why 'thābit' is used instead of 'wājib' for ada. This is a usul principle: supererogatory acts are commanded but not obligatory.
The author explicitly states that ada covers both obligatory and supererogatory acts.
3
Examine the metaphorical usage
Understand how each term can be used for the other, and why this is permissible: shared attribute of delivering to the one who deserves.
The analogy with 'lion' for a brave man is given.
4
Trace the dispute on the cause of qada
For rationally understood acts, does qada require a new cause? State the two views and their proofs, and identify the Hanafi majority position.
The passage presents two views: new cause vs. same cause as ada.

فصل الاتیان بالماء صور به نوعان مامور بہ کا لانا اور پورا کرنا اور اس کا وجود میں لانا دو قسم ہے ایک ادار یعنی جو شتی ثابت بالامر ہوئی ہے اسی کا عین حوالہ کرنا یعنی بعینہ وہی شتی لانا جو ثابت بالامر ہوتی ہے دوسرا قضاء جو واجب بالامر ہے اسی کی مثال پیش کرنا قلنا فی الاول ادام کی تعریف میں ثابت بالامر کا لفظ استعمال کیا ہے واجب کا لفظ نہیں بولا کیونکہ ادا جیسے واجبات میں ہوتی ہے ایسے نوافل میں بھی اور نوافل وسنن کا ثبوت بالامر تو ہے وجوب تو نہیں ہے اس لئے لفظ ثابت بولا تاکہ تعریف ادام نوافل کو بھی شامل ہو جائے بخلاف قضا کے یہ صرف واجبات کی ہوتی ہے اس لئے اس کی تعریف تسلیم مثل الواجب بہ کہا لفظ واجب کا استعمال کیا ويطلق كل منهما على الآخر مجاز یعنی ہر ایک کا اطلاق ایک دوسرے پر ہوتا ہے یعنی اطلات قضاء على الاداء واطلاق الاداء على القضا جیسے فاذا قضيتم منا سلم اور فاذا قضيت الصلوۃ میں اطلاق قضاء علی الاداء ہے اور ادیت الدین اور نویت اداء ظهر الامس یہاں ادا کا اطلاق علی القضا ہے ان دونوں امثلہ میں تسلیم مثل الواجب ہے اور یہ اطلاق مجاز شرفی کے طور پر ہے کیونکہ دونوں معنی ایک دوسرے کے مباین ہیں صرف تسلیم الشتى الى من يستحقہ میں اشتراک ہے اسی وجہ سے اطلاق ایک دوسرے پر مجازا ہوتا ہے۔ اطلاق المبائن على المبائن بسبب الاشتراك في الوصف مجازہ کا طلاق الاسد على الانسان بالاشتراك في الشجاعة والقضاء يجب بسبب جديد عند البعض اگر قتضا مثل غیر معقول ہو تو اس میں اختلاف نہیں بلکہ بالاتفاق بسبب جدید ہوتی ہے البتہ قضا بمثل معقول میں اختلاف ہے کہ اس کا وجوب سبب جدید کے ساتھ ہے یاکہ جو سبب ادا تھا وہی سبب قضا ہے تو عبد البعض سبب جدید کے ساتھ قضا واجب ہوتی ہے لان القربة یہ ان کی دلیل ہے حاصل یہ کہ یہ معلوم و معروف ہے کہ قریة و عبادہ اپنے وقت مقررہ ہی میں قربت اور عبادۃ قرار پاتی ہے ناذافات شرف الوقت جب وقت والی شرافت فوت ہو گئی تو اب اس قریہ کی مثل بغیر نص جدید کے معلوم نہیں ہو سکتی لہذا نص جدید کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ د عند عامة اصحابنا ہمارے اکثر اصحاب کے نزدیک یجب الى القضاء بما أوجب الاداء یعنی جس نص نے ادا کو واجب کیا ہے اسی کے ساتھ قضا واجب ہے لانه لما وجب بسببه کیونکہ
Chapter: The bringing into existence of what is commanded is of two types: one is ada (performance), which is the exact referral of that which is established by the command, i.e., bringing exactly that thing which is established by the command. Second is qada (making up), which is that which is obligatory by the command, presenting a similar example. We said in the first: in the definition of ada we used the term 'established by the command' (thabit bil-amr) and did not say 'obligatory', because ada occurs in obligatory acts as well as supererogatory (nawafil) acts, and nawafil and sunan are established by the command but are not obligatory. So we used 'thabit' to include nawafil in the definition of ada. In contrast, qada is only for obligatory acts, so in its definition it is said 'delivering the like of what is obligatory' (taslīm mithl al-wājib bih), using the word 'obligatory'. And each of them is used metaphorically for the other, i.e., applying qada to ada and applying ada to qada. For example, in 'fa-idhā qadaytum manāsikakum' and 'fa-idhā quḍiyat al-ṣalāh', qada is used for ada. And in 'adaytu al-dayn' and 'nawītu adāʾ ṣalāt al-ẓuhr', ada is applied to qada. In both examples, it is delivering the like of what is obligatory, and this application is metaphorical (majāz sharafī) because the two meanings are mutually exclusive; they only share in 'delivering the thing to the one who deserves it'. For this reason, applying one to the other is metaphorical. Applying one mutually exclusive thing to another due to shared attribute is metaphorical, like applying 'lion' to a man due to shared courage. And qada is obligatory due to a new cause according to some. If qada is of an unintelligible type (like a ritual act whose rationale is not understood), there is no difference; by consensus it is due to a new cause. But qada of an intelligible type is disputed: is its obligation with a new cause or is the cause of ada the same as the cause of qada? According to some, qada is obligatory with a new cause, because nearness (qurba) is their proof. The summary: it is known and well-established that an act of worship (qurba and ʿibāda) is considered a means of nearness only in its prescribed time. When the honor of time is lost, then the like of that act of worship cannot be known without a new text, so a new text is necessary. And according to the generality of our companions (most of us), qada is obligatory by the same text that obligated ada, because since it was obligatory by its cause...
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage is a legal definition section (fAṢL) on the two ways of fulfilling a commanded act: ada (original performance) and qada (making up after the time). The author first defines ada as the exact bringing of what is established (thābit) by the command, deliberately using 'thābit' instead of 'wājib' to include supererogatory acts (nawāfil) which are established by the command but not obligatory. Qada is defined as delivering the like (mithl) of what is obligatory (wājib). Then the passage explains the metaphorical usage: sometimes the word 'qada' is used for actual performance, and 'ada' for making up, as shown in Quranic examples and daily usage. This metaphorical usage is based on shared attribute of delivering something to its deserving recipient. The discussion then moves to a secondary issue: whether qada requires a new cause (sabab jadīd) or is obligated by the same cause as ada. For acts whose rationale is not understood (taʿabbudī), scholars agree a new cause (like a new command) is needed. For rationally understood acts (maʿqūl), there is a dispute: some say a new cause is needed because the time-based honor is lost, while the majority of Hanafis hold that the same cause that obligated ada also obligates qada, because the obligation persists until fulfilled, unless there is indication of dropping.

Key Terms
اداء (adāʾ): Bringing exactly what is established by the command (thābit bil-amr) in its proper time.
قضاء (qaḍāʾ): Performing the like of what is obligatory after its specified time.
ثابت بالامر (thābit bil-amr): Established by the command; includes both obligatory and supererogatory acts that are commanded.
مجاز (majāz): Metaphorical usage; applying a word to something other than its original meaning due to a shared attribute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the definition of ada use 'thābit bil-amr' (established by command) instead of 'wājib' (obligatory)?
A) To exclude supererogatory acts
B) To include supererogatory acts, which are established by command but not obligatory
C) Because qada is only for obligatory acts
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
Ada and qada are distinct legal concepts; their metaphorical interchange does not erase their technical differences, and the Hanafi school holds that qada is obligated by the same cause as ada.
